The Montreux Conference: Draft New Convention Passes First Reading; Meeting Adjourned until after the League of Nations Meeting; Soviet Union's Demands Gain Support from Three Countries; Only Japan Opposes at Present

Montreux: The Montreux Conference continued its meeting this morning and passed the first reading of the draft new convention proposed by Turkey. Article 9 of the draft stipulates that warships of all countries wishing to pass through the Dardanelles and Bosphorus straits shall obtain the permission of the Turkish government in advance and shall also notify the League of Nations. During the discussion of this case, the Japanese representative, Ambassador Sato to France, rose to speak, saying that in addition to obtaining the permission of the Turkish government, it was sufficient to notify the other signatory countries and that there was no need to notify the League of Nations. The chairman, Bruce, the Australian Commonwealth Special Envoy to England, said that since the new convention had to be registered with the League of Nations, the notification procedure was necessary. Sato replied that Japan's final position on this matter would be explained at the next meeting. The meeting was then adjourned until after the League of Nations General Assembly and the Administrative Council meeting were concluded. The French representative, former Minister without Portfolio Peng Gu, flew back to Paris after the meeting so that he could attend the French Senate's discussion of foreign policy. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

Montreal: The Soviet Russian representative's request to allow Soviet Russian warships in the Black Sea to freely enter and leave the straits, which was made during the conference considering Turkey's request to amend the Dardanelles Straits Convention, is now supported by Turkey, Romania, and France, according to various opinions. Among the great powers, only Japan opposes it so far. It is expected that Bulgaria will also oppose it, while Yugoslavia will demand that all countries enjoy equal rights in the straits. Unexpectedly, Ciano will represent Italy at the conference after the sanctions are lifted. It is expected here that Ciano will also strongly oppose the demands of Soviet Russian Foreign Commissar Litvinov. The conference will be adjourned today until after the special session of the League of Nations General Assembly concludes. Soviet Russian representative Litvinov reiterated yesterday at the plenary meeting the Soviet Russian request for special treatment. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

Montreal: At today's plenary session of the Dardanelles Straits Conference, Soviet Russian Foreign Commissar Litvinov reiterated the request for special treatment. Litvinov suggested that the clause prohibiting submarines from passing through the straits should also apply to aircraft carriers. French delegate Peng Gu advocated allowing countries fulfilling their obligations under the League of Nations Covenant to have greater freedom to pass through the straits. Japanese delegate Sato stated that Japan was prepared to accept the restrictions on warships sailing to the Black Sea if they were also applied to warships leaving the Black Sea. British delegate Stanhope reserved his opinion on Turkey's suggestion to limit the tonnage of warships passing through the straits to 14,000 tons. Turkish delegate Rushdi said that the Turkish government did not insist on this figure and would consider reasonable amendments. Litvinov proposed an amendment to the French suggestion to allow warships of belligerent countries to pass through the straits when fulfilling obligations under the League of Nations Covenant or under agreements concluded within the League of Nations framework, but agreed to make changes at Peng Gu's request. All discussions will continue tomorrow, but the plenary session will have to be convened after the League of Nations General Assembly is held. (Reuters dispatch, 26th)

The Positions of Various Countries Are Clearly Defined

Montreux, Switzerland: A special dispatch from our diplomatic correspondent states that the Montreux Conference has been in session for three days. Looking back at the past three days, the positions of the countries involved are now clearly visible. They are described below:

First, judging from the draft new convention proposed by Turkey, it can be seen that Turkey and Russia have the same objective, which is to restrict the free navigation of the Dardanelles and Bosphorus straits, so as to effectively blockade the Black Sea and prevent countries that are not Black Sea littoral states from entering and leaving at will. In this regard, Soviet Russian Foreign Commissar Litvinov spoke eloquently at the conference, and his words were exactly the same as those of the Soviet representative at the 1923 Lausanne Conference. In Russia's view, the geographical situation of the Black Sea should be given special attention. On the one hand, its gateway must be blockaded to prevent warships of countries that are not Black Sea littoral states from entering. On the other hand, this narrow strip of water should be reserved as a free passage for the fleets of Black Sea littoral states. This is the country's traditional policy, and Litvinov's words are intended to inherit the legacy of his predecessors and reiterate it. Romania is also a Black Sea littoral state and naturally has the same sympathy. Therefore, Foreign Minister Titulescu of that country has vigorously supported the views of the Soviet Union.

Second, as far as Britain and Italy are concerned, the two countries are quite close to each other at the Montreux Conference. According to recent statistics, the total tonnage of Italian merchant ships passing through the two straits ranks first among all countries. If free navigation is restricted, Italy will suffer a hundred disadvantages without a single benefit. In Britain, the proposal to strictly regulate and restrict navigation is also opposed, and the establishment of a special system to benefit the Soviet Russian navy is like a thorn in its side and cannot be agreed to. Britain and Italy have the same interests, so they exchanged friendly glances and felt mutually sympathetic. However, up to now, Britain has expressed dissent internally, but externally it has only put forward reservations of a general nature and has not hastily determined its position. Its attitude is obviously to wait for Italy to express itself on the following two points: 1. The Soviet Union should not enjoy special privileges regarding navigation of the two straits. 2. Japan is currently not a member of the League of Nations and should not be allowed to restore any relationship with the League of Nations.

Third, judging from the remarks made by the French representative Peng Gu yesterday, it can be seen that France does not want to oppose the views of Russia and Turkey, but believes that if some countries have an obligation to go to war for common purposes in the future due to regional mutual assistance agreements or League of Nations resolutions, they must have the right to freely pass through the two straits, whether in wartime or peacetime, and must not be restricted in any way. The French position is viewed by Premier Léon Blum and Foreign Minister Yvon Delbos of the cabinet as follows:

In terms of quantity, Japan aims to ensure the security of its national defense in an unrestricted state and ensure complete freedom in terms of quality, and should prepare effective armaments suitable for its national conditions. From this point of view, it was decided not to participate in the treaty. As for the legal aspect, it is natural not to comply with the oath in fact. Because the Imperial Navy did not participate, the U.S. Navy resumed the 16-inch matter, which is a natural consequence of the provisions of the treaty. It is also said that after receiving the official reply from the Imperial Government, the three countries, Britain, the United States, and France, will begin deliberations. Now that there is no need for the three countries to deliberate, the situation when Japan and Italy do not participate in the new treaty is anticipated and codified, so it does not seem to be a problem. (Allied dispatch, 25th)

Important Speech by the British First Lord of the Admiralty: Stresses Strengthening Naval Power; Fulfills Responsibility for Collective Security; Learns Two Lessons from Past Experience; Expresses Sympathy for Anglo-American Cooperation

(London) First Lord of the Admiralty Hoare said in a speech at the Royal Empire Society tonight that some people think that war is inevitable, which is a guilty and foolish thought. However, Europe is now full of flammable fuel. Although no country wants to declare war, if powerful countries like Great Britain do not have military strength sufficient to make their power felt in the pursuit of peace, then a spark can turn into a prairie fire. For this reason, the British government must once again do its best to speed up the British naval program. If the British army, navy, and air force can be properly strengthened in time, then there will be no world war. Hoare went on to say that in the midst of the changes caused by air power, we can create a fleet commensurate with our strength, which can defeat the enemy and open the seas, and can sail to any place to fulfill its three major responsibilities, namely, the protection of cruising transport. The naval staff and I are never so foolish as to say that our defenses are sufficient to cope with attacks and have more than enough. But if someone asks if the advent of air power has changed the navy's mission and we cannot create a fleet that can fulfill its traditional responsibilities, I will answer "yes." My advisors and I are determined to make full use of air power to build this fleet, so that the new fleet can be in a superior position and become the most easily mobilized peace force in the world. We have learned two lessons from the past six months. One is the practical application of collective security, namely, the British fleet permanently stationed in the Mediterranean. The British fleet and collective security are two in one and one in two. Although the British fleet in the Mediterranean and the Red Sea did not have the convenience of mobilization and did not make careful preparations, it was able to fulfill its entrusted responsibilities faithfully and effectively in dealing with the worries of disturbance, the stagnation of international affairs, and the danger of delay, and its prevention of the spread of the Italo-Abyssinian War can be said to have been completely responsible and without regret. The second lesson is that in theory, the military strength of 50 countries is invincible, but in practice, the value of this military strength depends entirely on whether each country is not only willing to go to war with the aggressor, but also prepared to fight with the aggressor when it attacks. Among the member states of the League of Nations, only Great Britain is prepared to do this, and even to make effective preparations. In today's state of world public opinion, can Great Britain think that it can rely on the cooperation and assistance of distant countries and those whose main countries are not members of the League of Nations? All these lessons show that the League of Nations' reliance on Britain's powerful navy is one of the major elements of peace, which is no different from the world in the 19th century.

Furthermore, the failure to realize collective military action last autumn shows that although the British Empire will do its best to accomplish the doctrine of collective security, it still depends on the defense of the empire, allowing it to be a strong British navy. This lesson should be calmly and quietly pondered by both the country and the autonomous territories. Although there are such changes today, the fundamental fact that the empire's life depends on its maritime communications still exists. We should learn wisdom from the lessons of the past six months. We are determined to prevent the influx of war. The future naval power of our country will be stronger than in recent years, so our power to pursue peace will inevitably increase rather than decrease. Hoare concluded by saying that he found the article in the United States Naval Institute Proceedings calling for Anglo-American naval cooperation to make war impossible interesting and sympathetic. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

Japan Refuses to Participate in the London Three-Power Naval Treaty; Naval Authorities Explain Their Views

(Tokyo) Because the Imperial Government decided not to participate in the British, American, and French naval treaty, the most important point of the treaty's qualitative restrictions, the stipulation that the caliber of main guns on battleships should be 15 inches, became a dead letter. The proviso in the latter part of the clause will take effect immediately and 16-inch guns seem to be under careful consideration. However, a glimpse can be seen in the foreign policy declaration issued by Imperial Navy Minister Osami Nagano in both the House of Representatives and the House of Peers a few days ago. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a telegram from Ambassador Sato, who is attending the Montreux Conference, asking for instructions regarding the Turkish government's request. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs sought the opinion of the Ministry of the Navy on the 24th. As a result of the meeting of leaders of the Ministry of the Navy, it was decided to take a firm attitude. The Japanese Navy expressed sympathy for the Turkish government and would do its best to revise the straits system. However, the Turkish government's request to impose excessively lenient restrictions on Soviet Russian warships sailing from the Black Sea to the Mediterranean Sea and to lack parity with the restrictions on foreign warships is something that should be corrected. However, Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations and cannot cooperate with the League of Nations to bear the obligation of ensuring the safety of the straits. This point must also be clearly stated. (Allied Press dispatch, 25th)

(London) According to news from Tokyo, the Japanese cabinet has decided to refuse to sign and join the naval treaty signed by Britain, France, and the United States. However, it is reported that Fujii, the Japanese chargé d'affaires in England, has not yet notified the Foreign Office of this decision. People in political circles do not find Japan's attitude unusual. What is attracting attention at this moment is only what intentions the country holds in the future. In other words, what will the country's future trend be? Will it comply with the treaty's restrictions in practice, even though it refuses to sign and join it in principle? Or will it ultimately take actions that violate the treaty? The general public now hopes that Japan will act with moderation and that its refusal to join the treaty is only for the purpose of formality, to preserve the country's prestige, and has no other intention. In particular, the British, French, and American naval treaty stipulates that the maximum caliber of main guns on battleships is 14 inches, and this restriction is conditional on Japan accepting it before January 1, 1937 (the date on which the three-power naval treaty comes into effect). Therefore, if Japan's attitude does not change by the end of this year, the impact will be that at least the caliber of main guns on battleships will increase from 14 inches to 16 inches. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

The Explanation of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement Has No Major Differences

(London) When the House of Commons met today, a member asked to state the points of disagreement in the interpretation of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement. First Lord of the Admiralty Hoare replied that he was happy to tell the members that all the details had been resolved satisfactorily and amicably and that there were no major differences in the interpretation. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

The United States Changes Three Small Pacific Islands into Colonies; Preemptive Strike Against Britain to Open Air Stations

Honolulu: The U.S. government has officially made Baker, Jarvis, and Howland Islands U.S. colonies and is moving U.S. citizens to live there. It is generally believed that the purpose of this move is to preempt Britain. There are now twelve U.S. students being transported to the islands by coastal patrol boat from Honolulu, with four people staying on each island and raising the U.S. flag on them. It is said that when a Honolulu-to-New Zealand air route was recently planned, the proposal to use the three islands as aircraft stops was noted by many. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

Marconi and Alosi Promoted from Naval Lieutenant Commander to Rear Admiral

(Rome) It was learned today that Marconi, the inventor of the radio, and Sir Alosi, the chief Italian representative to the League of Nations, have recently been promoted from naval lieutenant commander to naval rear admiral. (National dispatch, 24th)

League of Nations Administrative Council to Hold Extraordinary Meeting Today; King of Abyssinia Travels from England to Geneva, Intending to Appeal to the League of Nations for Justice

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council is scheduled to hold an extraordinary meeting at 5:00 PM the day after tomorrow. The meeting will be chaired by British Foreign Secretary Eden. French Foreign Minister Delbos is also expected to attend for the first time in his life. The Italian delegation will remain absent. The agenda for the extraordinary meeting of the Administrative Council is as follows: The issue of the Assyrian and Chaldean minority settlements in Iraq, a British mandate territory; The issue of filling vacancies for German Judge Schücking and American Judge Kellogg at the Permanent Court of International Justice; The Locarno Treaty and the re-entry of German troops into the Rhineland; The issue of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia. (Havas, 25th)

(London) The King of Abyssinia departed for Geneva today. Those who saw him off shouted, "Good luck!" and "God bless the King!" The King responded solemnly. Before his departure, the King expressed his deep gratitude to the British people for their sympathetic support. The Abyssinian embassy released a summary of the conversation between the King and British Foreign Secretary Eden on June 23, in which the King expressed his intention to vigorously oppose the lifting of sanctions against Italy in Geneva and to urge the League of Nations to take more forceful measures against Italy to uphold justice. (Reuters, 25th)

(London) The King of Abyssinia departed from Victoria Station for Geneva at 2:00 PM today. The British government does not intend to send representatives to see him off. Official sources have stated that the British government does not send representatives to greet or see off foreign heads of state traveling in a private capacity. (Havas, 25th)

British and French Foreign Ministers Set Off for Geneva; Eden Makes a Brief Stop in Paris En Route

(London) With the League of Nations meeting imminent, the discussion on abandoning the sanctions policy against Italy will be adopted and implemented. The discussion on the reorganization of the League of Nations will also be submitted for discussion by a majority of member states. The opening act of this drama, watched by all, will unfold here. The Cabinet is scheduled to meet this morning to give Foreign Secretary Eden final instructions, which will serve as his guide as he represents Britain in negotiations. After receiving his instructions, Eden is scheduled to take a plane to Paris this afternoon. Upon arriving in the French capital, he will meet with French Prime Minister Blum and Foreign Minister Delbos to exchange views. In addition, the Emperor of Abyssinia is also scheduled to depart for Geneva at the same time. It is reported that the Emperor will not personally engage in activities, but will maintain close contact with the Abyssinian delegation to the League of Nations. The Swiss Federal Government has notified the Emperor to refrain from residing in Switzerland until the Italo-Abyssinian dispute is resolved. Therefore, the Emperor intends to leave Switzerland after the conclusion of the League of Nations General Assembly and live in seclusion in the countryside, most likely near Brighton in England. (Havas, 25th)

(Paris) Foreign Minister Delbos is scheduled to take a train to Geneva at 9:20 PM tomorrow to attend the extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations Administrative Council. Prime Minister Blum may travel to Geneva by road on Saturday of this week to attend the extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations General Assembly. (June 30) (Havas, 25th)

Sovereignty of the Bahrain Islands Usurped by Britain; Iran Lodges Second Protest with the League of Nations

(London) The Bahrain Islands, located near the Arabian Peninsula in the Persian Gulf, are claimed by the Iranian government as its sovereign territory but have been seized by Britain. Iran has already lodged a protest with the League of Nations and has recently filed a second protest. British officials are not surprised and believe that this protest is unrelated to the recent visit of the Sheikh of Bahrain to London. Its motivation is due to the British government recently exchanging documents with the government of Hejaz in the name of the Bahrain government, stipulating that goods passing through the Bahrain Islands are subject to transit taxes levied by the authorities of the islands. (Havas, 25th)

Italy and Germany Seeking Closer Ties in Military Technology; Italian Undersecretary for Aviation Makes Surprise Visit to Berlin

(Rome) Lieutenant General Valle, Undersecretary of the Air Force and Chief of Staff of the Army, flew to Berlin yesterday. The local newspapers had kept the news secret beforehand and did not publish any reports before his departure. Only this morning was a Berlin dispatch released, stating that Lieutenant General Valle had arrived in the German capital. Political figures have offered some explanation for the purpose of Valle's visit, stating that the visit focuses on technical matters, while the political aspects are minimal. He is scheduled to visit various German aircraft factories and airfields today, accompanied by officials from the Nazi Party, and inspect the entire organization of the German Air Force. The closer ties between Italy and Germany in aviation technology are a prelude to a coordinated diplomatic policy. Since the start of the Italo-Abyssinian War, the governments of Germany and Italy have been working towards this direction, as can be seen from the similar tone of their newspapers. Furthermore, it is rumored that the Italian Fascist Party plans to send representatives to attend the Nazi Party congress in Nuremberg in September of this year, and the National Fascist Student Association is also advocating for sending 500 students to Berlin in August to attend the Olympic Games. (Havas, 25th)

(Berlin) Upon arriving here, Italian Undersecretary of Aviation and Chief of Staff of the Air Force, Lieutenant General Valle, immediately went to the Ministry of Aviation, where he was received by Secretary General Milch. Diplomatic sources believe that the reason General Goering avoided meeting him was because Hitler wanted to prevent a backlash from British public opinion, and therefore instructed officials to treat General Valle's visit with caution. (Havas, 25th)

Germany's Huge Military Spending; 900 Million Pounds This Year - British Newspaper Publishes Figures

(London) The Morning Post has published figures on Germany's military rearmament expenditures, calling it "the first time such detailed figures have been published." According to the report, the maintenance costs of the German army, navy, and air force in 1935 totaled £240,000,000, while the basic cost of rearmament ranged from £400,000,000 to £500,000,000. The maintenance costs for the army, navy, and air force in 1936, this year, totaled £500,000,000, with the basic cost of rearmament remaining the same as last year. Combining the two, military spending for this year totals £900,000,000. (Havas, 25th)

Representative to the Hague Court; Poland Nominates Zheng Tianshi to Fill Wang Chonghui's Vacancy

(Geneva) Poland has nominated Dr. Zheng Tianshi as China's representative to the Hague International Court to succeed Wang Chonghui. Dr. Zheng once served as Acting Minister of Justice and recently served as the Chinese Commissioner for the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London, earning a high reputation. (Reuters, 25th)

New Japanese Ambassador; Yoshida Visits the British Foreign Office; Scheduled to Present Credentials Today

(Yokohama) The British Consul General in Yokohama, Mr. Hamilton Holmes, has served in Japan for forty years and has now decided to retire. He is scheduled to return home on the Canadian liner on July 31 from Yokohama. Foreign Minister Arita and Minister of the Navy Osumi believe that he has made significant contributions to Anglo-Japanese friendship and have decided to present him with a pair of silver vases as a souvenir to express their gratitude. Japan Actively Implements Economic Policy Towards China; Ministry of Finance Dispatches Inamori to China

(Tokyo) In order to actively implement national economic policies and economic policies towards China, the Ministry of Finance has decided to establish a new section within the Minister's Secretariat. At the same time, it has decided to station a secretary in China. It has now selected Inamori Minoru, an official in the Foreign Exchange Control Department, as the secretary stationed in China. The formal order will be issued next month. (Domei, 25th)

Yoshizawa Ordered to Go to the US; Adjusting Japan-US Relations; Scheduled to Depart at the End of This Month

(Tokyo) Former Foreign Minister and Member of the House of Peers Yoshizawa Kenkichi is scheduled to depart from Yokohama for the United States on the Taiyo Maru on the 29th. While his ostensible mission is to represent Japan at the sixth general meeting of the Pacific Relations Conference to be held in North America this summer, in light of the complex and delicate state of Japan-US economic relations today, the overall adjustment of these relations has been carefully considered by the Foreign Minister since taking office. Ambassador Kurusu in Belgium was instructed to visit the US government and various key figures to negotiate and build understanding upon his arrival in the US. This time, former Foreign Minister Yoshizawa Kenkichi was persuaded to come forward to lay the foundation for adjusting Japan-US relations. Therefore, after attending the conference from August 15 to 29, he will visit Washington and New York to meet with President Roosevelt, Secretary of State Hull, and other business leaders to frankly exchange views on the current state of Japan-US economic affairs. The results are expected to be considerable. Regarding his decision to go to the United States, Yoshizawa told reporters at his home in Azabu, "I am just a wanderer. I cannot achieve much by going to the United States. Please do not have extravagant expectations." He is scheduled to depart from Yokohama on the 29th of next month. However, his actions after arriving in the United States have not yet been decided. However, since he is going to the United States, he naturally intends to visit Washington and New York. However, when and with whom he will meet, and what he will discuss, will all be decided after he arrives in the United States. Therefore, the date of his return is also difficult to predict. (Domei, 25th)

US Navy Petty Officer; Case of Leaking Military Secrets; Charged with Violating the Espionage Act; Accused with a Japanese Person

Los Angeles: Retired U.S. Navy officer Thompson and Japanese Navy Major Miyazaki have been charged with violating the Espionage Act and secretly reporting information about national defense to Japan, with a total of nineteen counts. Thompson is already in jail. It is now believed that Miyazaki fled back to Japan before the authorities began investigating the leakage of details about the Pacific Fleet's large-scale maneuvers and warship armaments. (Reuters, 25th)

Los Angeles: A federal court judge today filed a public lawsuit for espionage against retired U.S. Navy Petty Officer Thompson and a Japanese person. This case attracted considerable national attention a few days ago because secrets of U.S. naval artillery were allegedly sold to foreigners. Federal law enforcement officers have detained Thompson here and prohibited him from communicating with the outside world. However, the whereabouts of the Japanese person are still unknown. It is rumored that the Japanese person has already fled back to Japan. The charges listed in the lawsuit are divided into espionage and conspiracy, totaling fifteen counts, including statements that documents, records, codes, signals, drafts, photographs, drawings, maps, "models, instruments, and information about national defense were all smuggled to Japan and sold to a Japanese official, etc., and that this action clearly harmed the interests of the United States." According to peacetime custom, he should be sentenced to four years in prison and a fine of 20,000 yuan. According to reports, the Japanese person is a colonel in the Japanese Navy who promised to pay Thompson a monthly salary, in addition to allowances, with a maximum amount of 300 yuan. These payments were transferred through the Yokohama Bank in San Francisco. (Kokumin, 24th)

Belgian Prime Minister Announces Policy Platform; Major Reforms to Be Implemented in Society and Economy; Foreign Policy Remains Unchanged

Brussels: The Chamber of Representatives held its first meeting this afternoon, attended by Prime Minister Janson, who delivered a policy statement outlining the government's plans for large-scale reforms in society, the economy, politics, and the parliamentary system. Regarding society, the Cabinet's proposed plan includes the following three points: Establishing a minimum wage; Granting workers a certain number of days of paid annual leave; Implementing a 40-hour work week in factories where working conditions are harmful to health. In addition, the Cabinet also plans to expand the scope of compulsory education to reduce unemployment. "However, in order to implement this plan, various measures must be promoted in the economic and financial fields, such as reducing deposit and loan interest rates, converting foreign debt, and regulating banks." Regarding politics, the Cabinet intends to implement the various clauses contained in the Constitution - the freedom and rights granted to the people by the Constitution must be fully protected and must not be infringed upon. Regarding the electoral system, the Cabinet plans to reduce the number of representatives in the Chamber of Representatives "to strengthen executive power and stabilize the position of the Cabinet. The Cabinet will not immediately resign if a Cabinet proposal is rejected by the Chamber of Representatives, and will only resign in special circumstances, such as when the budget is rejected." Finally, regarding foreign policy, Prime Minister Janson only stated that the current Cabinet will follow the previous Cabinet's policies. After the Prime Minister finished speaking, Labor Minister Troclet presented three draft laws in accordance with the three points of the Cabinet's proposed social issues: Granting workers a certain number of days of paid annual leave; Increasing wages; Implementing a 40-hour work week in factories where working conditions are harmful to health. (Havas, 24th)

British Cotton Cloth; India Reduces Tariffs; Major Blow to Japanese Dumping

Shimla: The Indian government issued a proclamation on the 24th stating that the revised cotton yarn and cloth tariff proposal of the Cotton Yarn and Cloth Tariff Inquiry Committee will be implemented from the 25th. This applies to British goods, while Japanese and other foreign goods will remain the same. The content of the revised tariff for British goods is as follows (old tariff rates in parentheses):

Coarse cotton cloth: 20% ad valorem or 3.5 annas per pound (25% ad valorem or 4.375 annas per pound); Coarse cloth with borders, printed cloth, twill, etc.: 20% ad valorem (25% ad valorem); Cotton yarn: same as before. (Domei, 25th)

Japan's Trade War with Australia; Implements the Trade Protection Law; Claims It Can Control Australia's Fate

(Tokyo) The government published an imperial ordinance in the official gazette on the 25th, launching the Trade Protection Law against Australia, which took effect immediately. (Domei, 25th)

(Tokyo) As a result of Japan's launch of the Trade Protection Law against Australia, trade relations between the two countries have virtually been severed, and an intense trade war is inevitable. As a result, Japan's export trade to Australia will naturally decrease. However, Japan imports 23 million yuan worth of wool and wheat from Australia each year. If Japan resists imports, it can control the fate of Australian farmers. (Domei, 25th)

Canberra: Australian Prime Minister Lyons made a radio address to the public today after hearing about the Japanese government's implementation of retaliatory plans for Australia's new tariffs, saying that Japan's move was deliberately intended to suppress Australia's trade policy. During recent contacts with Australian authorities, Japan stated that if Australia restricts the import volume of Japanese textiles and increases its import taxes, Japan would impose harmful restrictive clauses on Australian imports. However, the Australian government will not abandon its determination to protect Australian industry and maintain trade between Britain and Australia. Everything is now under consideration, but the Australian government does not want to hastily implement plans to resist Japan. (Reuters, 25th)

US Democratic Convention; Robinson Attacked the Republican Party Vigorously; Committee Met Overnight to Consider Party Platform

Philadelphia: Senator Robinson, chairman of the National Democratic Convention last night, spoke out against the Republican Party's platform and promised to focus on the plank advocating a return to the gold standard. Robinson asked the Democratic Party members to fight with confidence, to which the crowd responded with enthusiastic cheers. After Robinson finished his speech, the conference declared a recess, but the subcommittee continued to meet overnight to resolve the difficulties of the party platform. (Reuters, 25th)

Philadelphia, USA: The Democratic National Convention has quickly completed all temporary organizational procedures today and is preparing to discuss the platform and nominate a presidential candidate.

Philadelphia, USA: The Democratic National Convention has quickly completed all temporary organizational procedures today and is preparing to discuss the platform and nominate a presidential candidate. In fact, the behind-the-scenes work has already been arranged. The delegates are meeting only to express the importance of the convention. Although the platform committee has received many suggestions throughout the day, all major issues have been predetermined. William Green, president of the American Federation of Labor, demanded a reduction in the Supreme Court's power to invalidate congressional legislation, because in the past two years, the Supreme Court has repeatedly ruled the National Recovery Act and other laws invalid, preventing the government from limiting minimum wages, maximum working hours, and appropriate working conditions. Green also represented labor in demanding that the Democratic Party support a 30-hour work week, continue public works, raise wages, protect labor organizations, and continue the New Deal's social security plan. O'Neal, president of the American Farm Bureau Federation, also presented eleven rural programs, such as controlling agricultural products, managing currency, reducing industrial product taxes, and restricting patents. The biggest point of contention was New York Governor Lehman's demands for wages and hours, because they were more stringent than those advocated by President Roosevelt. Regarding the monetary system, a platform has been drafted, supporting the principle of discretionary systems, and stating that the government will respond at any time according to changes in the financial situation. However, it did not mention restoring the gold standard, or immediately trying to establish international currency stability. Party leaders have expressed satisfaction with this platform, and it is understood that it does not intend to include Senator Thomas's proposal to increase the issuance of silver certificates to inflate the currency and raise prices. At the same time, the southern states opposed amending the convention's constitution to change the eligibility for presidential candidates from a two-thirds majority to a simple majority. This opposition was raised to the Rules Committee by Congressman Cox, but the committee did not take any action, so this point of contention will probably also be submitted to the convention for discussion. (Kokumin, 24th)

Communist Party Presumed Candidate

(New York) The Ninth National Convention of the Communist Party of America, which was recently held here, was chaired by party leader Foster, who delivered a speech. He first congratulated the French left-wing Popular Front on seizing power, calling it a "glorious victory," and argued that a strong Popular Front should also be organized within the United States, hoping that it would develop and grow to resist the reactionary behavior of the Fascist and militarist factions. Foster then attacked the "conservatives," saying that these people were trying to deprive the people of their inherent democratic rights and civil liberties. The fact that the "Black Robe Party" and the "Ku Klux Klan" can continue to exist and run rampant in the country is the fault of the "conservatives." These people now feel embarrassed by the people's protests and are using an irresponsible oligarchy as a talisman, which is the Supreme Court. According to reports, Foster has now been nominated by the Communist Party as a candidate for the general election, and this is the third time he has participated in the presidential race. Marseille, France; Seamen's Strike Ends; Labor and Management Reach Agreement

Marseille, France: The striking sailors have reached an agreement with the shipping companies. All French ships in the port sounded their horns simultaneously at 8:25 PM yesterday for fifteen minutes to indicate the end of the labor unrest. (Havas, 25th)

Marseille: The strike of the sailors of the seventy French ships, who "remained on board but did not work," has ended today. The ships sounded their horns to express their joy. According to a representative of the seamen's union, all the demands of the seamen have been accepted by the employers. The striking sailors who remained on board each ship are expected to leave tomorrow. Before the strike ended, although the French government warned foreign ships not to enter Marseille, the ships of the British Company continued to enter and leave the port of Marseille without changing their sailing schedules. The Getúlio Vargas will arrive in Marseille on Friday from Japan. The weekly express train from London to catch the Kaiser-i-Hind sailing from Marseille will depart as usual tomorrow. Palestine; British Troops Engage in Clearing Villages; Again Attacked by Armed Arabs

Jerusalem: Today, when a squad of British soldiers searched an Arab village near Jerusalem, the Arabs suddenly opened fire on the British soldiers. The British soldiers immediately returned fire, killing two Arabs and wounding three others. Recently, trains on the railway line between Jerusalem and Jaffa have been attacked by Arabs, so the British soldiers are engaging in clearing the villages. At the same time, three houses were found in the Tulkarm area containing unused military supplies, which were destroyed by the British soldiers, and nine Arabs were arrested. (Reuters, 24th)

New Constitution of Southern Ireland; Abolishes the Position of Governor-General; Replaced by a Publicly Elected Representative as Head of State Ceremonial

Dublin: Eamon de Valera, President of the Executive Council of the Irish Free State, announced in Parliament today that the position of Governor-General would be abolished in the Free State's constitution. De Valera made this announcement when presenting the Governor-General's budget in Parliament, and said that a publicly elected representative would now replace the Governor-General as head of state ceremonial. The Governor-General of Southern Ireland is the direct representative of the British monarch and receives an annual allowance of 10,000 pounds. The current holder of this position is Mr. Bickley, who took office in November 1932. (Reuters, 24th)

Following France's Lead: Dutch Bank Reduces Discount Rate

(London) Yesterday, the Bank of France reduced its discount rate, and today, the Dutch Bank also lowered its discount rate from 4.5% to 4%. Well-informed circles in the foreign exchange market here are not surprised by this, considering it purely an act of imitation, as Dutch capital has virtually stopped flowing out. As for the Bank of France, it is widely believed that the reduction in the interest rate should not be seen as a sign of progress in France's financial situation; it is merely a gesture by the French government to reassure the people. Furthermore, since taking office, the French government has been waiting for an opportunity to implement a cheap money policy, which is an important part of the government's agenda, as evidenced by the upcoming issuance of "baby bonds." Fuzhou Merchants Sanction Smuggled Goods: Silk and Cloth Guild Prepares to Prevent Sales, Banking Guild Restricts Loan Security

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Minhou County Chamber of Commerce and various trade guilds previously telegraphed the Ministry of Finance requesting a strict investigation of smuggled goods in order to protect the national economy. The Ministry of Finance replied that the government had already established various measures for smuggling and strictly ordered active prevention. From now on, all industrial and commercial enterprises only need to advise each other not to purchase and sell smuggled goods, and smuggling will naturally disappear. To eliminate smuggling relies entirely on the self-exertion of all industrial and commercial enterprises. For self-protection, it is also their own inescapable responsibility to prevent the encroachment of smuggled goods. The Chamber of Commerce has distributed circulars to various trade guilds to inform them. It has been found that the smuggled goods in this province are mainly textiles, foreign goods, and sugar. They mostly enter Fuzhou through the coastal areas of Fuqing, Putian, Changle, and Lianjiang. Dishonest industrial and commercial people, tempted by low costs and high profits, inevitably purchase smuggled goods. Recently, the silk and cloth industry has been auctioning goods, displaying prices, and distributing price lists in the market. The so-called Indian silk, flower silk, and yarn varieties are only ten cents per foot, suggesting that they are purchasing smuggled goods with low costs. Because the authorities are about to take action, the person in charge of the industry guild is concerned that there may be profit-seeking people among the colleagues, and if the facts are true, they will inevitably face criminal penalties. A special notice is issued to colleagues, advising them not to purchase goods without bills of lading and tax receipts. Measures for prevention, supervision, and reporting are being discussed. At the same time, the newly established Fuzhou Banking Guild has also resolved to unanimously refuse to mortgage smuggled or tax-evading goods. All merchants who want to pledge goods for loans must have customs tax receipts as proof before they will be accepted. As for the Provincial Tax Inspection Office, in the past week, it has uncovered a total of 26 smuggling cases in the coastal ports, including 387 and a half cases of foreign oil, 285 packages of white sugar, 27 boxes of tea, 37 packages of fertilizer powder, 15 bolts of rayon, and more than 400 jin of rayon, as well as other groceries, salted fish, fruits, matches, and drugs. They have been reported to the provincial authorities.

Continuous Heavy Rainfall in Northeast: Flood Situation Serious; Railways Washed Away, Traffic Blocked; Communications Cut, Victims Awaiting Rescue

Harbin Correspondence: Continuous heavy rainfall in various parts of Northeast China has led to an extraordinarily serious flood situation. Railways have been washed away, blocking traffic. Floods have overflowed, inundating farmland over a wide area. At a time when the Japanese puppet regime is imposing harsh policies, this situation is creating a sentiment of both divine and human resentment, which should not be underestimated. According to the information on the flood situation from the Harbin Puppet Railway Bureau, the details are as follows:

Water Situation on the Labin Line

At noon on June 17th, the bridge pier of the Xilang River (between Shanhetun and Ping'an) on the Labin Line suddenly sank due to being submerged and impacted by the water. The second bridge was washed away, and the third pier was also tilted. Currently, train passage is impossible. In addition, the Hulan River, a tributary of the Xilang River on the Labin Line, has also overflowed. The bureau's residences and villages within Ping'an Station have been completely flooded, and residents are flocking to the station to take refuge. Also, because of the overflowing of the Lalin River and the Hulan River tributary, train services between Sijiafang, Liudaoling, and Shuiquanliu Ping'an, and Dujia and Shanhetun stations have been completely suspended since 9 AM on the 18th, causing the 101st passenger train, which departed from Harbin on the 16th (at 3:20 PM), to be forced to stop between Sijiafang and Liudaoling, unable to proceed. The Railway Bureau immediately dispatched a rescue train from Wuchang, stopping between Shuiquanliu and Ping'an to carry out emergency rescue. Regarding the flood situation in the aforementioned areas, the 103rd train, which departed from Harbin on the 17th, stopped at Shanhetun Station and could not proceed. The 101st train, still between Sijiafang and Liudaoling, returned to the Wuchang side. As of the 18th, trains departing from Harbin only reached Wuchang. Also, from 3 PM on the 18th, telephone communications south of Wuchang were completely cut off, and the entire situation is completely unclear. It is expected that the entire restoration work will take at least twenty days.

Disaster Situation on the Binsui Line

At 5 AM on June 18th, the roadbed near Lengshan, Shitouhezi, and the 1161 kilometer mark on the Binsui Line was washed away by water. Therefore, the 971st passenger train departing from Mudanjiang and the 901st passenger train departing from Suifenhe were stopped at Hengdaohezi, unable to proceed. Also, near the 1102 kilometer mark between Yimianpo and Wanshan, the river overflowed, and trains could not operate. Telephone communications east of Yimianpo have also been completely cut off. Rescue trains have been dispatched from the Yimianpo Railway Engineering Section to the dangerous locations affected by the flood for emergency rescue. However, due to the disruption of telephone communications, subsequent news is also completely unclear.

Planes Deliver Food

The Labin Line, now entirely submerged, and the areas near Ping'an and Liudaoling, the Harbin Railway, the Jilin Railway Bureau, and related Japanese authorities are currently negotiating to deal with reconstruction and rescue efforts. As for rescue trains, due to the complete disruption of telegraph and telephone communications, and the volume of water constantly increasing, its momentum is quite violent, and is forming a huge disaster. To this day, the Japanese puppet regime still has no appropriate solution. Currently, in order to buy people's hearts, they are promoting rescue operations for the disaster victims, first using aircraft to survey the disaster situation and then using aircraft to transport food to relieve the victims. However, the number of victims is extremely large, and the amount of food transported by aircraft is very small, a drop in the bucket, and is of no practical help.

Datian Falls and is Quickly Recovered: Zhang Kewu's Bandits Occupy City for Three Days and Nights; Flee City Upon Hearing of Approaching Army

Xiamen Correspondence: The bandits Zhang Kewu and Zhang Chengfu, originally from Dehua, recently fled back to their old nest in the western mountains of Dehua from Xianyou and Yongtai. On the 13th and 14th, the Zhang bandits gathered more than 1,000 scattered bandits from the four counties of Dehua, Xianyou, Yongtai, and Datian, raising the fake banner of the "First Route Army of the Chinese Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army," with Zhang Kewu and Zhang Chengfu proclaiming themselves as division commanders. On the 18th, they launched an all-out attack on Datian in three routes. The two Zhangs each led one route, attacking the northeast of Datian. The former puppet battalion commander Tu Feifeng, led more than 200 men, attacking the south of Datian from Shanpingtou in the west of Dehua. On the 18th, they came into contact with more than 100 men from the squad led by squad commander Tan Maogong of the provincial security regiment, outside the south gate of Datian city. More than 100 men from the Datian County Security Team defended the northeast gate. After fierce fighting until night, most of the bandits continued to arrive and surrounded the county seat. The defending troops were vastly outnumbered. Squad commander Tan Maogong was killed in action, and the county seat was captured by the bandits at 11 PM on the 18th. The telephone line between Dehua and Datian was cut off by the bandits, and communications were lost. They also occupied the postal and telecommunications agencies in Datian. County magistrate Zhang Duanqiao led county government personnel and a portion of the county security squad, retreating through the north gate when the bandits captured the city. After the bandits entered the city, they immediately demanded 20,000 yuan from the Chamber of Commerce and all shops in the city. Because the county magistrate had fled, there was no leader in the city. Zhang Kewu then appointed a city gentleman to serve as county magistrate, but no one dared to accept. Regiment commander Peng Tang of the security regiment heard that bandits were spying on Datian and quickly led his troops from Dehua to reinforce. Upon arriving at the border between northern Dehua and Datian, he learned that the city had fallen. Later, because of the large number of bandits and Peng's troops numbering less than a thousand, he dared not advance rashly, and temporarily defended northern Dehua, preventing the bandits from returning. Datian mail also only reached Chishui Town in Dehua. At the same time, the Huang Su unit of the security regiment was ordered to reinforce Yongde. Huang then led a large detachment from Yongtai through Shuikou, Nanting, and Xishan, arriving in Dehua city on the 20th. Regiment commander Peng Tang returned to the city on the same day and discussed with Huang the method of suppressing the Zhang bandits. Soon after, they received an order from the Provincial Security Department, and the detachment of the regiment and the detachment of the regiment were all placed under the command of Huang Su. On the 21st, they launched a multi-pronged attack on Datian. Brigade commander Han Wenying led his troops, departing from Yongan for Datian on the 18th and arriving at Taoyuan on the 21st, only a hundred li from the county seat. Also traveling with them was a battalion of the 83rd Division's advance team. Upon hearing that the main army was about to arrive, Zhang Kewu abandoned the city at 11 PM on the 21st and fled back to Guiyang, on the border between Dehua and Yongchun. The Datian county seat was then retaken on the morning of the 22nd by the security regiment and the regiment. In total, the Zhang bandits occupied the city for three days and nights. After Huang Su and Peng Tang entered the city, they immediately handled the aftermath. The telephone line between Dehua and Datian was repaired on the 23rd. County magistrate Zhang Duanqiao's whereabouts were still unknown as of the 23rd, after he retreated from the county seat. The brigade departed from Taoyuan and arrived at Datian County on the 23rd. At the same time, the military strength of Yongchun, Dehua, Datian, and Xianyou was very strong, and the Zhang bandits were in danger of being surrounded. Councilor Zhu was sent by the Security Department, arriving in Dehua on the 20th, to recruit Zhang bandits. Zhu sent Ke Jiefu, the former chief of staff of Zhang Xiongnan, to Datian on the 21st, to contact Zhang Kewu and Zhang Chengfu. After the Zhang bandits retreated to Guiyang, Ke reported back that they were willing to be incorporated, but the specific methods have not yet been determined (June 25th).

Third Year

Estimated costs: Temporary expenses: 463,500 yuan; Annual recurring expenses: 99,600 yuan; Monthly recurring expenses: 8,300 yuan.

Decline of Agricultural Sidelines in Zhangzhou: From 5 Million Yuan Annually to 2 Million Yuan; Rural Cooperation is Being Planned for Relief

Xiamen Correspondence: Zhangzhou, located at the mouth of the Jiulong River, has fertile land and abundant water resources, making it the best agricultural production area in southern Fujian. In addition to rice, agricultural sidelines such as fruits and sugar cane are also abundant. In the past, items such as sugar cane, oranges, pomelos, lychees, longans, and daffodils had an annual production value of over 5 million yuan per county. Among these, besides sugar, oranges are the famous "Fuzhou oranges" of Shanghai, pomelos are "Pishan pomelos," and lychees and longans are considered unique products of southern Fujian. Daffodils are even more uniquely produced. However, in recent years, due to the dumping of foreign goods and smuggled goods, these special products have been greatly affected, dropping from over 5 million yuan to over 2 million yuan. According to a survey by the Longxi Office of the Rural Cooperation Committee, comparing the quantity and value of various agricultural sidelines in Longxi in 1926 and 1935, there was a difference of more than half: Sugar: In 1926, the production volume was 500,000 dan, worth 3.5 million yuan. In 1935, the production volume was 100,000 dan, worth 600,000 yuan, a decrease of over 80%. In the early years of the Republic, there were 36 sugar factories, but later, due to the dumping of foreign sugar, the production of local sugar sharply decreased, and the sugar factories closed down. Red oranges: In 1926, the production volume was 150,000 dan, worth 450,000 yuan. In 1935, the production volume was 400,000 dan, worth 1.2 million yuan, an increase of over 160%. Pomelos: In 1926, the production volume was 100,000 dan, worth 400,000 yuan. In 1935, the production volume was 50,000 dan, worth 200,000 yuan, a decrease of 50%. Lychees: In 1926, the production volume was 50,000 dan, worth 250,000 yuan. In 1935, the production volume was 30,000 dan, worth 150,000 yuan, a decrease of 40%. Longans (i.e., dried longans): In 1926, the production volume was 50,000 dan, worth 250,000 yuan. In 1935, the production volume was 10,000 dan, worth 50,000 yuan, a decrease of 80%. Daffodils: In 1926, the production volume was 100,000 cages, worth 400,000 yuan. In 1935, the production volume was 10,000 cages, worth 80,000 yuan, a decrease of 80%. According to the above statistics, the value of sideline products in 1926 was still 5.25 million yuan, while in 1935, it was only 2.28 million yuan. In order to gradually provide relief, the office has formulated a product sales cooperation plan: (A) The Farmers Bank of China will provide special product sales funds. (B) Improve production technology, supply production materials, reduce costs, and sell products to avoid selling at low prices and directly supply consumers. (C) Consolidate the credit and sales cooperatives that have already been established. Nine sales cooperatives and sixty-four credit cooperatives have been established, and new cooperatives will be developed. Sales cooperatives will be organized in areas where there are more than 100 producers or an annual production of more than 10,000 yuan (there are currently over 70 villages in special product areas that have not yet formed cooperatives). (D) Guide the organization of joint cooperatives. Special product loans are divided into: Sowing loans; Advance loans; Loans are repaid during the harvest and sale period of the products. (June 21)

Beijing: Special Internal Debt, Fourteenth Lottery for Principal Repayment

Beijing News: The Beijing Special Construction Public Bond held its fourteenth lottery for principal repayment on the 24th. Representatives from the Audit Department, Zhong Shurong; the Ministry of Finance, Dong Puming; the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Mu Huaxuan; the Foundation Management Committee, Shen Zuomei; and representatives from the Central, Zhongnan, and other banks in Beijing were present. The meeting began at 2:00 PM as scheduled. First, Secretary-General Wang, the chairman, gave a report, stating that the total amount of the public bond issued was 3 million yuan. Thirteen lotteries have been held, with a principal repayment of 1.95 million yuan and an interest payment of 1.032 million yuan. This lottery will repay 150,000 yuan in principal and 42,000 yuan in interest. Although the public bond fund was established at a time when the municipal treasury was extremely tight, each lottery for principal repayment and interest payment has been allocated in advance. The principal and interest to be paid in this lottery have been allocated to the Foundation Management Committee in accordance with regulations and deposited in various custodian banks. The vehicle tax that guarantees the principal repayment and interest payment of this public bond currently generates more than 180,000 yuan per quarter, or more than 360,000 yuan every six months. After allocating the funds to the fund, there is still a surplus, which is sufficient to show the stability of the credit of this public bond. Then, the supervisors checked the ledger of the winning numbers, and the lottery began. Five numbers were drawn: 94, 46, 74, 65, 31. Payment will begin on June 30.

Changshu: Road Worker Rapes and Kills Young Girl

The case of robbery by road workers on Yangfu Road at the current port has not yet been resolved, and now a case of gang rape and murder of a young girl has occurred in Jincun. Caijin, the 20-year-old daughter of Jin Xiaodi, a farmer in Tongdangba, Jincun, had four or five road workers break into her home on the Dragon Boat Festival and demand rice dumplings. At that time, Jin was working in the field, and only Caijin was left at home to guard the house. The workers, seeing that the girl was defenseless, committed their bestial gang rape, which eventually led to her being on the verge of death. They then used needles to prick her arms. A neighboring girl noticed and ran to tell her father, who returned home and saw the situation. By evening, Caijin had died of exhaustion. Jin Xiaodi recognized the faces of the road workers and arrested Xue Asan, Jiang Dahong, Yang Asi, Zhang Abao, Wang A'er, and others, sending them to the county for investigation. According to the workers' confession, they admitted to the gang rape. On the Dragon Boat Festival, they went to the Jin family to buy rice dumplings and suddenly saw the girl (the deceased) lying unconscious on the bed. After Xue Asan examined her, he said she had heatstroke. Because he knew a little about acupuncture, he used a sewing needle to prick her to relieve the heatstroke. She was once awake. When her father returned home, he did not know the reason and accused them of raping and killing her. In fact, the girl died at midnight. The official ordered an autopsy for further verification and set the 25th to take a steamboat to the countryside for the autopsy. The workers were all taken into custody.

Changzhou: Spring Cocoon Production Increases Sharply

This year's spring silkworms in Wuyi have aroused great interest among farmers. However, due to the high price of leaves, the price of cocoons sold only covers the cost. Fortunately, the cocoons are in good condition, and the results are not bad. The cocoon businesses have now been completed. According to statistics from the Silkworm Improvement District, the county has raised a total of 160,400 spring silkworm cards, each of which can produce 35 catties of cocoons, equivalent to 13 catties of dry cocoons. The total cocoon production is over 19,300 dan, nearly double that of last year. The silkworm industry improvement fee that can be collected is over 87,000 yuan, and 60,000 yuan has already been collected. The autumn silkworm cards for this year have already been ordered and will be closed on July 10. It is estimated that the county needs cards. The Improvement District has ordered 60,000 cards from various seed production farms, with a selling price of 45 cents per card.

Jiaxing: Strict Collection of Old Taxes

The Jiaxing County Government, under orders to pursue overdue old taxes, has established a Tax Collection Office to summon and detain households owing taxes. Those who are unable to pay are being detained, causing widespread complaints. Some, fearing the ferocity of the tax collectors and unable to pay, have even committed suicide. The authorities, however, insist on adhering to the law and dare not be negligent. Although various legal groups have appealed for a postponement of the collection, the pursuit is even more severe than before. Currently, over 400,000 yuan of old taxes have been collected in the county, leaving the people impoverished. Upon learning of this, the provincial government has sent Wei Songtang and others to Jiaxing to investigate the rural situation for review. It is learned that Wei and others have completed a clear investigation and returned to the province to report.

Hangzhou: Measures for Establishing Agricultural Warehouses Determined

The Zhejiang Construction Department is preparing to establish agricultural warehouses in various counties. Experts led by Xu Yuanruo were dispatched to various counties in eastern and western Zhejiang to investigate warehouse locations. The work has now been completed, and a report on the cooperative warehouse establishment measures between the Construction and Civil Affairs Departments has been submitted to the province. On the evening of the 24th, the heads of the two departments met and determined the locations of five major warehouses: Yueqing, Pingyang, Jinhua, Linhai Haimen, and Haining Xiashi. The county-level warehouses will allocate one-third of the local grain reserves, converted to cash, for warehouse construction expenses. Each county will set up two to ten locations, using the grain reserve warehouses for agricultural warehouses. Small warehouses will temporarily use existing temples and other buildings as a principle. The large warehouse locations will conduct trial runs of small and medium warehouses simultaneously. The large warehouses require construction costs of 500,000 yuan and will be borrowed from the Shanghai Bank. The small warehouse expenses are planned to be borrowed from the Farmers Bank of China or the Agricultural and Industrial Bank. The plan will be launched in fiscal year 1936.

Ningbo: Hangzhou-Ningbo Section Launches Special Express Train

In order to facilitate travel on the Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, it is planned to add a special express train. It is learned that the railway bureau has decided to implement this from July 15. The departure time has been changed to 7:45 AM from Ningbo, arriving in Cao at 10:10 AM, which connects with the Cao-Shao-Xiao Road bus. It can arrive in Hangzhou around 12:00 noon. However, the five small stations of Zhuangqiao, Hongtang, Yejia, Zhangting, and Shushan will not be stopped at in order to increase speed. The original early-morning local train running between Ningbo and Ci has been extended to Yuyao, departing from Ningbo at 6:55 AM.

Nantong: Fierce Battle Between Police and Bandits in Yuxi

In the Yuxi area of Tongyi, bandits have been rampant recently. The police team was dispatched to suppress them and encountered bandits in Minsheng Township. The bandits opened fire and resisted. One bandit was killed, and one policeman was also shot and killed. The bandits used the sorghum fields for cover and retreated westward. They are currently being pursued.

Full Text of the Draft Agreement on Factory Inspection in the Public Concession Published

Establish an Inspection Office to Enforce Chinese Factory Laws; Fessenden Says Implementation by July 1 is Not Possible

Municipal Council Applied to the Consular Body for Recognition Yesterday

Central News Agency reports that Mayor Wu believes that the factory inspection issue in the concessions has been delayed for too long, and disasters have occurred repeatedly, endangering the lives of workers. Factories with poor equipment especially affect workers' health. Therefore, he has consulted with the central government to find a solution as soon as possible within the scope of preserving China's sovereignty. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun has also negotiated with Fessenden, Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession. Both sides have now formulated a draft solution, the content of which is that the Municipal Council recognizes that factory inspection in the concession is based on the authorization of the Chinese government and complies with Chinese laws. The Chinese authorities, on the other hand, recognize the special circumstances within the concession. Half of the inspectors will be recommended by the Municipal Council, but the established inspection office will fully comply with Chinese factory laws, factory inspection laws, and other relevant laws when performing its duties. Violators will be punished through court trials, and the qualifications of inspectors will also be strictly defined. The plan was approved by the Municipal Council Board of Directors on the 24th, but it is heard that the Japanese side has expressed opposition, or it may still need to be discussed by the Consular Body. The municipal government will formally submit it to the central government for approval. The implementation procedures and steps are said to still require Secretary-General Yu and Fessenden to negotiate.

Full Text of the Agreement: Draft Agreement on the Implementation of the Factory Law in the Shanghai Public Concession (Revised June 15, 1936) 1. The Chinese authorities authorize the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession to implement the Factory Law and its implementing regulations, as well as other relevant factory inspection laws, that have been implemented in the Chinese area and are agreed upon by both parties through negotiation from time to time, within the Public Concession. 2. A Factory Inspection Office will be established within the Municipal Council. Half of the inspectors will be appointed by the Chinese authorities and half by the Municipal Council. 3. Inspectors should possess the following qualifications: (A) Proficiency in Chinese and English; (B) Familiarity with the Chinese Factory Law and its implementing regulations; (C) Possession of knowledge or experience in any of the following fields: industrial chemistry, architectural hygiene engineering, electrical engineering, mechanical engineering, statistics, or other experience applicable to factory inspection. 4. Each inspector should be on probation for six months before formal appointment. 5. Inspectors' salaries will be determined based on their qualifications and experience. 6. The above-mentioned Inspection Office should perform its duties in accordance with the Chinese Factory Inspection Law. 7. In cases of violations of the law, when the Chinese Factory Law needs to be enforced, a complaint should be filed with the court. 8. The Municipal Council should submit reports to the Chinese government in accordance with procedures to be agreed upon separately. 9. This agreement is valid for three years. Either party may notify the other party six months prior to the expiration date to terminate it.

Consular Body Meeting: A reporter from New Voice learned yesterday that the Municipal Council applied to the leader of the Consular Body, the British Consul-General in Shanghai, Sir Brenan, yesterday morning, attaching the full text of the agreement. Yesterday afternoon, Mr. Lang, secretary of the Consular Body, told a reporter from New Voice that the Consular Body received the application for recognition from the Municipal Council this morning (i.e., yesterday morning) regarding the draft agreement on the implementation of the Factory Law in the Shanghai Public Concession. It is not yet decided when the Consular Body meeting will be held, nor is it certain whether it is necessary to hold a meeting for discussion. This matter may not necessarily go through meeting procedures, and it may be approved by each consul separately. If a meeting must be convened, it can be held within a week.

Implementation Pending: Fessenden, Director-General of the Municipal Council, also stated that although the draft agreement has been approved by the Municipal Council Board of Directors, it cannot be formally signed at this time because it still needs to be recognized by the Consular Body. Last time, I signed the document with Mr. Yu Hongjun, but it was not formal. When the formal signing procedure is held in the future, it will be carried out by formally appointed representatives of both parties. It is feared that it will take a considerable amount of time, and it will not be possible to start implementation by July 1.

Other Information: Article 3 of the draft agreement only stipulates that half of the inspectors will be appointed by the Chinese authorities and half by the Municipal Council. The exact number of half is not stated. However, according to foreign sources, the number of inspectors is specified as four Chinese and four foreigners, and there is a rumor that Ms. E. Hiuder, the current director of the Industrial Section of the Municipal Council, will be in charge of the matter. The agreement also does not disclose the source of funding, but it is said that it will be borne equally by both sides. It is also learned that once the agreement on the implementation of the Factory Law in the Public Concession is signed and implemented, Secretary-General Yu Hongjun of the municipal government will continue to negotiate with the French Concession authorities to conclude an "Agreement on the Implementation of the Factory Law in the Shanghai French Concession." Because there is a precedent to follow, the solution will be easy.

Loan Association Continues to Issue Small Loans

Over 10,000 Yuan in Loans Approved

The Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee held its thirty-first meeting at the China National Products Bank on Tianjin Road at 4:30 PM on the 24th. Committee members present included Cai Zengji, Zhang Peishen, Xi Demao (representing Zhang), Chen Guangfu (representing Cai), Song Ziliang, Qin Runqing, and Yu Zuoting (representing Qin). Chairman Cai Zengji reported on routine committee matters. Thirty-four applications for small credit loans were submitted. After review and decision, one loan was approved at the original requested amount, one was approved at half the original requested amount, and thirty-two were reduced. A total of 10,300 yuan in loans was approved. Additionally, five applications were rejected because either the business operations did not comply with the loan principles or the loan request did not comply with the regulations. All approved cases will be notified to the respective applicants by the committee. It was also reported that many recent loan applicants have not complied with Article 9 of the established principles, which states, "The loan amount shall not exceed half of the capital." The requested amount often exceeds or equals the declared capital. It is hoped that in the future, when companies and shops needing loans obtain application forms from the committee's office on the second floor of the National Products Bank on Tianjin Road, they should send a responsible person or the owner himself to facilitate detailed inquiries and avoid errors.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway and Others to Implement Intermodal Transport on Three Routes

Intermodal Freight Transport Limited to Four Types of Goods Initially; Trial Period of Six Months Starting July 1st

The Huainan Railway, Jiangnan Railway, and Beijing-Shanghai/Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have reached an agreement to implement intermodal passenger and freight transport on these three routes. The scope of passenger intermodal transport is temporarily limited to third-class one-way and round-trip tickets and luggage parcels. Regardless of whether the tickets are one-way or round-trip, the fare for all three routes will be charged at 85% of the standard third-class fare. If a special express train is required, the additional express train surcharge should be paid according to regulations. As for the scope of intermodal freight transport, it is temporarily limited to whole-car shipments of wheat, rice, rapeseed, and soybeans. For the two main lines and the Jiangnan Railway, except for soybeans, which are charged at the current fifth-class freight rate and are subject to the intermodal decreasing rate for longer distances, the remaining three items are calculated according to the intermodal special rate and are not subject to the decreasing rate. On the Huainan Railway, all items are charged at the fifth-class freight rate and are subject to the decreasing rate. The two main lines and the Jiangnan Railway will initially only handle arrival shipments, not originating shipments. Yaohuamen and Wuhu Riverbank Station will serve as connecting stations for intermodal transport. The two main lines have temporarily designated six stations: Zhenjiang West Station, Wujin, Wuxi, Wuxian, Shanghai North Station, and Hangzhou. The Jiangnan Railway is only a transit route and does not have intermodal transport stations. The Huainan Railway has temporarily designated ten stations: Tianjia'an, Datong, Huainan Mine, Hefei, Zhonggan, Chaoxian, Cuozhen, Xiatangji, Jiong Yanghe, Qiaotouji, and Yuxikou. The intermodal transport period will begin on July 1st of this year and will be a trial run for six months. After the trial period, further negotiations will be held to continue the operation.

To develop transportation, the China National Aviation Corporation is planning to open a Sichuan river route, departing from Chongqing and passing through Luxian, Xufu, and Jiading, directly reaching Chengdu.
