Japanese Newspaper: Kawagoe's China Policy

Different Shades from Previous Ambassadors

The Foreign Affairs Review translated from the Shanghai Mainichi Shimbun says that the arrival of Kawagoe, the new Japanese ambassador to China, is of great significance in how to break the deadlock in Sino-Japanese relations. Since landing on the 22nd, the ambassador has briefly outlined his China policy. These are, of course, fragmentary glimpses, but it is not difficult to see the foundation of the ambassador's plans. What we should pay particular attention to is that the ambassador's aspirations for China seem to place more emphasis on economics than politics. This is slightly different from the style of previous ambassadors to China. The adjustment and development of Sino-Japanese relations based on this approach are also something that both countries cannot help but hope for. But what exactly is the nature of Ambassador Kawagoe's economic aspirations for China?

According to the specific content of Ambassador Kawagoe's economic aspirations for China, as expressed on various occasions before and after his arrival in China, it seems to lie mainly in railway construction and the survey and development of mining. Railway construction is a very urgent issue in China, and it goes without saying. China, a country with vast land and abundant resources, has had its materials buried in the ground and the development of various industries delayed due to the lack of railway construction. In addition to the economy, political unification is also waiting for a long time to achieve. Railway construction is the most urgent of urgent tasks. China itself knows this best. Japan's cooperation in this matter, under certain conditions, can undoubtedly be said to be beneficial to China. Cooperation, since Japan does not have funds to lend, refers to the provision of materials and technology. If China uses the materials provided by Japan to carry out railway construction, it would be a great plan for the long term with great benefits. The so-called minor details of conditions and other aspects are merely issues that have not yet been addressed. We believe that in the near future, if Ambassador Kawagoe proposes this issue, it would be wise to accept it without doubt. Secondly, the survey and development of mining is also a very important issue for China, just like railways. The iron ore in Henan and Fujian, the petroleum in Shaanxi, the antimony in Hunan, the manganese in Hunan and Guangxi, and the coal in North China all have unlimited reserves underground. This can also provide sufficient and large-scale exports. Cooperation with Japan in this area is also mutually beneficial.

Ambassador Kawagoe's economic aspirations are as described above, which is quite beneficial to both parties. If the Chinese side has sincerity in promoting Sino-Japanese cooperation, then even if there are some differences on specific details, the overall outline should certainly be acknowledged.

Suppression of Opium in Concessions Urgently Needs to Proceed; Ma Liang Visits Mayor Yesterday

Our Side Hopes for Cooperation from Concession Authorities in Investigation and Suppression; Over 10,000 Opium Addicts in Shanghai Have Quit

The suppression of opium in the concessions, after the Opium Suppression General Supervisory Department of the Military Commission separately instructed the Shanghai Commissioner's Office and the Municipal Government to discuss the matter, Opium Suppression Inspector Ma Liang visited Mayor Wu at the Municipal Central District yesterday morning to discuss implementation methods. The municipal opium suppression agencies are working hard on opium suppression in order to eradicate it within the set timeframe. Details are as follows:

Inspector Visits Mayor Wu: Ma Liang, Opium Suppression Inspector and Director of the Shanghai Office of the Opium Suppression General Supervisory Department of the Military Commission, after receiving the order from the Supervisory Department, went to Beijing the day before yesterday to meet with the authorities and request instructions on how to implement opium and drug suppression work in the concession areas. He returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday. Inspector Ma visited Mayor Wu at the Municipal Central District at 10:00 AM yesterday morning to discuss with the Public Concession's Municipal Council and the French Concession's Board of Directors the various implementation methods and steps for opium and drug suppression.

External Correspondence: According to inquiries made by the Dagongbao reporter to the municipal opium suppression agencies, our side hopes that the concession authorities will not abandon their preconceived notions of sovereignty. While they claim to be assisting on the surface, they have not made any concrete expressions of cooperation, making it difficult to achieve practical results in implementation. The Opium Suppression General Supervisory Department of the Military Commission is eliminating these difficulties by requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to send a note to the ministers and consulates of the countries related to the two concessions, requesting their sincere assistance in cooperating with our side in carrying out opium and drug suppression work. They plan to jointly establish a similar opium and drug suppression agency within the possible scope of not hindering sovereignty.

Opium Addicts Who Have Quit: The Municipal Public Security Bureau released information on opium suppression work, including: 1. The number of opium addicts who renewed their permits in the second phase, from April 1st to June 23rd, was 18,141. 2. The number of opium addicts who reapplied for their opium quitting certificates from May 10th to June 20th was 5,295. 3. The number of opium addicts who have quit, from July to December 1935, was 5,397; from January to May 1936, was 5,060, totaling 10,457 opium addicts who have quit. There are also 700 to 800 people still in various opium quitting hospitals.

District Inspections: Because the deadline for renewing opium permits in the second phase has been extended to the end of this month, with only five days left until the deadline, the Municipal Public Security Bureau has dispatched all personnel from the inspection division to various districts to work with the local branch bureaus and district offices to step up inspections. Those who have not renewed their permits by the second deadline will be sent to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for strict investigation. Government employees who smoke opium have also been instructed by the police bureau to quit quickly, otherwise they will be investigated and prosecuted according to the law.

The North-China Daily News reports that yesterday, a reporter from the North-China Daily News spoke with Dr. Jourdan, Director of the Public Health Department of the Public Concession, about the different regulations in Britain and Shanghai regarding the sale of prohibited drugs and showed him advertisements published in pharmaceutical magazines. It stated that, according to the 1933 Medicines and Poisons Act, certain medicines are not allowed to be sold except with a doctor's prescription. The list includes products advertised for sale in Shanghai newspapers, which the authorities have not taken action to suppress. Dr. Jourdan replied that Shanghai has a special status, so it is currently inconvenient to implement the new regulations governing the sale of poisons. To implement these new regulations, one must have a team of qualified inspectors to regularly check whether pharmacies are complying. However, the current economic situation of the Municipal Council does not allow for the establishment of such inspectors. One must also force all doctors to register. Although this measure was submitted to taxpayers as a regulation as early as 1906, it was not approved. The authorities are now carefully considering the whole problem. However, Shanghai has several unique difficulties that cannot be easily eliminated unless they are rejected by public opinion. Moreover, Shanghai is an international city with its own unique problems.

Qingdao Branch of the Federation of Labor Unions Sends Personnel to Shanghai to Investigate Smuggled Goods

And to Discuss Prevention Measures, Will Depart in Three Routes

The Qingdao Branch of the Shanghai Chinese General Federation of Industry is sending personnel to Shanghai to investigate and penalize smuggling. Details are as follows:

Sending Personnel to Investigate: Due to rampant smuggling in North China and the authorities' lack of preventive measures, the Qingdao Branch of the Chinese General Federation of Industry has sent Chairman Yin Zhizhong, Executive Zheng Wenzheng, and Executive Committee Member Huang Wenshen to Shanghai yesterday to investigate the situation. They will divide into three routes to investigate: 1. Yin Zhizhong will go to the Yangtze River area, then to Sichuan, and then to Xi'an before returning to Qingdao. 2. Zheng Wenzheng will go to Beijing, then to Zhengzhou, and the Jinghan Road and Jinpu Road areas. 3. Huang Wenshen will go to the Jinghan and Longhai Road areas. In addition to investigating and preventing smuggling, they will also investigate commercial conditions in various locations.

Yin Zhizhong Speaks: According to the New Voice News Agency, a reporter met with Chairman Yin Zhizhong yesterday. According to him, smuggled goods in Qingdao are purely by land, transferred from Tianjin. Artificial silk and sugar are the most common. Due to special circumstances, people can only encourage it psychologically and cannot penalize it in reality. The Chamber of Commerce has also not been able to make any concrete expressions. Merchants are not affected, and the production industry suffers the most. Smuggled goods shipped to Qingdao are currently stockpiled and have not yet been sold. It is estimated that they account for more than twice the amount of imported goods. Qingdao is located in the commercial center of North China, with convenient land and water transportation and a special environment. Because political power used to belong to foreigners, people have a deep-rooted impression of buying and using foreign goods. Since the handover, although domestic products have gradually developed, there is a lack of specialized advocacy agencies, making it difficult to reverse people's psychology of loving foreign goods, resulting in sales difficulties and no way to buy domestic goods. If we want to reverse this decline, we must integrate the industry. Therefore, this association invites national factories to join, so that the group can be sound and develop slowly. In recent years, various industries have been declining. This summer festival, Qingdao is just maintaining the status quo. However, the stockpiling of smuggled goods and dumping in the second half of the year is very worrying. We will depart in separate routes soon and expect to return to Qingdao by the middle of next month.

University Presidents

Until June 30th of Next Year

Jianghai Customs issued Announcement No. 1523 regarding the continuation of surtax collection on customs duties, stating: "It is hereby announced that we have received an order from the Ministry of Finance stating that the 5% surtax currently collected by customs should continue to be collected until June 30, 1937. You are hereby ordered to comply accordingly. This is to inform all merchants so that they are all aware. This announcement is specially issued. Supervisor Tang Haian, Tax Bureau Director Ba Runsen."

City Chamber of Commerce Petitions the Legislative Yuan to Expedite the Commercial Registration Law

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted another petition to the Legislative Yuan, urging the implementation of the Commercial Registration Law. The original petition stated, "Regarding the petition for a matter concerning the regulations on joint and several liability for partnership debts, which is inconvenient for business practices, a request for modification was made. Since your esteemed Yuan accepted the request from the business community and adopted the proposal of eight legislative members, including Wu Kaixian, to separately establish the Commercial Registration Law to remedy the situation, Article 9 of the draft law clarifies the names and addresses of the partners and the types and amounts of investment. If each individual has registered with the competent authority in the place of business, they may be liable for sharing losses within the limit of their investment. The general business community then decided to implement this law to ensure compliance with national conditions and business practices, while also protecting the rights of both creditors and debtors. This is thanks to the grace of your esteemed Yuan, and we celebrate with joy. However, the draft law, after being submitted to the joint meeting of the Civil Law and Commercial Law Committees in October of the 23rd year, has been stalled to this day. During this period, the affiliated associations have sent telegrams to your esteemed Yuan three times, and the Secretariat replied each time stating that the matter had been referred to the Civil Law and Commercial Law Committees for reference, but the deliberation is still indefinite, and implementation is even more delayed. The affiliated associations have repeatedly received letters from the business community expressing their expectations and inquiries, and we are at a loss for words to respond. It is said that the law reflects the will of the people, and concerning the partnership liability, it should follow customary practices. For decades, the business community has been calling for this, as evidenced by the records, and there is no need to elaborate. It is said that the law should adopt the most progressive principles in the world, and our Civil Code's Law of Obligations takes benevolence, forgiveness, and fairness, protecting the spirit of the weak, as its guiding principles, as stated at the beginning of the document. The spirit of equal protection for creditors and debtors is indeed the most progressive characteristic of our commercial law, and it is also the origin of your esteemed Yuan's compromise and separate establishment of the Commercial Registration Law. Based on these reasons, there is no reason for the draft law to be shelved. If it is said that commercial activity is sluggish and many businesses are going bankrupt, and that increasing liability is necessary to protect the rights of creditors, then in the event of business liquidation when sharing partnership liabilities, each party can take care of their due responsibilities and not evade them in the slightest. Since the strict implementation of joint and several liability, incidents of evasion have been endless, and debts are difficult to recover, which is the unanimous opinion. Strict laws are not enough to prevent abuses but are more likely to enable them. Merchants have suffered greatly from this kind of lesson and are asking for change. The legislative authorities do not seem to need to adhere to their established policies. Therefore, the 7th Members' General Assembly of this session has resolved to again request your esteemed Yuan to promptly deliberate and implement the law. A further record is made to formally petition, hoping for your review and implementation for public convenience."

China Cottonseed Oil Factory Assembles National Technical Talent

Actively Preparing Oil Factories in Various Locations – Cooperation with Foreign Merchants Proceeding Smoothly

For the purpose of improving the production and sales of tung oil and other vegetable oil materials nationwide, the Ministry of Industry, together with the provinces of Sichuan, Hubei, Hunan, Anhui, and Zhejiang, initiated the organization of China Vegetable Oil Factory Co., Ltd., inviting government and business to jointly invest. Preparations have been underway for over a month now, and the progress has been repeatedly reported in various newspapers. According to sources, the factory is actively negotiating the equipment of oil factories in various locations and assembling technical talent from the national oil industry to jointly contribute to the success of the plan. The details are described below:

Recruiting Specialized Talent: The factory's improvement plan involves many technical issues. The originally determined work steps were only general policy guidelines, and detailed rules and methods need to be researched and planned by experts. However, the number of chemical and oil material experts in our country is limited, and many are already holding important positions. Therefore, it is necessary to seek talent widely. It is learned that the factory has requested various agencies and businesses to loan specialized talent, such as Zhang Weiru, He Tuan, Lin Tianji, Liu Hu, Wu Jinquan, Wen Xiangxing, etc. All responsible parties have agreed to assist the Vegetable Oil Factory. It is said that the above experts have extensive research on vegetable oil materials. Mr. Zhang is currently in charge of tung oil inspection in Chongqing and Wuhan. Mr. Lin studied tung oil drying theory at Cornell University Graduate School in the United States and obtained a Ph.D. After returning to China, he founded the tung oil inspection work at the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau and served as the director of the manufacturing department of the Shanghai Great China Match Company. He has written books such as "The Development of Tung Oil Industry in the United States and Britain," "The Inspection Method of Mineral Oil Mixed into Tung Oil," and "The Tung Oil Industry in China," and is a well-known tung oil expert in China. Mr. Liu majored in agricultural chemistry in the United States and interned at a tung oil factory in the United States. After returning to China, he worked as a technical worker at the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau and as a professor in the chemistry department of the Agricultural College of the Central University. Mr. Wu is a Ph.D. in chemistry from Stanford University in the United States and has been a chemistry professor at Zhejiang University for many years. He has written papers such as "Research on the Chemical Composition of Tung Oil" and "The Effect of Sunlight on Tung Oil." Mr. Wen was the director of the Wuzhou Tung Oil Factory in Guangxi and was responsible for technical work. Recently, he served as a technician at the Nanchang Oil Industry Management Office. The factory's preparatory office has asked Messrs. Lin, Liu, Wu, and Wen to go to Sichuan, Hubei, Hunan, Zhejiang, and other provinces to contact and assist in the preparatory work in those areas. It is also heard that the factory is continuing to seek experts, striving to assemble technical talent from all over the country to contribute to the cause.

Contacting Oil Factories and Oil Pools in Various Locations: Most of the oil factories and oil pools in various parts of our country for refining and storing tung oil are owned by foreign merchants. At the beginning of the preparation, the factory sent letters to overseas merchants in various locations, asking them to list the oil pools for reference. It is learned that the factory has obtained considerable cooperation from local foreign merchants, and some merchants have expressed their willingness to transfer their oil factories and oil pools. The factory is now sending personnel to Hubei and Hunan to contact them. Those who do not want to sell are also free to do so. However, when the factory establishes oil factories in various locations in the future, it will give priority to using existing equipment to protect the interests of merchants. If the existing equipment is insufficient, then additional equipment will be added. It is heard that branch factories are planned to be established in areas along the Yangtze River, such as Chongqing, Wanxian, Yichang, Shashi, Changde, Changsha, Hankou, Laohekou, Wuhu, and Hangzhou, to expand refining and storage and facilitate the business of oil merchants.

Establishment Meeting Postponed: In other news, China Vegetable Oil Factory Co., Ltd. originally planned to hold an establishment meeting in the capital on July 5th of this year. It is learned that although the factory's shareholding matters have been completed, the production areas in various locations are far away, and it takes time to contact them. Furthermore, oil merchants in various locations have requested to participate. Therefore, for the sake of caution and popularizing business shares, the date of the establishment meeting has been postponed. It is expected that it will be held in July.

City Chamber of Commerce Petitions the Ministry of Finance to Abolish the Harsh Taxes on Western Tobacco in Various Provinces

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday petitioned the Ministry of Finance, stating, "Regarding the petition for a matter based on the facts, according to a letter from the Western Tobacco Trade Association, our Western tobacco is produced in the Gansu Gaolan Jingyuan area and sold in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and the three northeastern provinces. In the past, the annual production and sales were about 30,000 dan, or 60,000 boxes, and the business value was about 5 million yuan. No less than hundreds of thousands of people directly and indirectly depend on it for a living. In recent years, due to rural bankruptcy and reduced purchasing power of the people, and after the September 18th Incident, the sales in the three eastern provinces were cut off due to the impact of counterfeit goods in Manchukuo. The annual business volume has decreased from 30,000 dan to more than 10,000 dan. All of these have been enough to put our industry in a precarious situation. Furthermore, various provincial governments along the route of tobacco transportation have levied various taxes on Western tobacco, each with its own name. In the most recent situation, in Gansu Province, for every 'shi' (two boxes), a public sales fee of 6 yuan, 4 fen, and 8 li must be paid to leave the city of Lanzhou. The eastern route, from Lanzhou to Shaanxi and onto the Longhai Railway, costs this amount. The northern route, from Lanzhou through Ningxia to Baotou and onto the Ping Sui Railway, costs 8 yuan, 4 fen, and 4 li. In addition, lijin on both the northeastern routes is 8 yuan, 4 jiao, 2 fen, and 4 li. Obligatory donations are 2 yuan, 8 jiao, 9 fen, and 4 li on the eastern route and 3 yuan, 2 jiao, 9 fen, and 7 li on the northern route. Stamp taxes are 5 jiao and 4 fen on each route. Transportation from Lanzhou, such as northward transport, passing through Ningxia, incurs a Ningxia transit tax of 4 yuan, 8 jiao, 9 fen, and 7 li per dan. Transporting by train from Baotou, passing through Datong, Shanxi, requires paying a Datong tax of 4 yuan, 4 jiao, 8 fen, and 8 li per shipment. As for the eastern route, starting from Lanzhou, passing through Jingchuan, incurs a tax of 9 jiao, 3 fen, and 4 li per dan, plus a supplementary tax of 1 yuan. Passing through Changwu, Shaanxi, incurs a tax of 1 yuan and 1 jiao, 2 fen per dan. Passing through Jingyang incurs a public sales fee of 2 yuan, 1 jiao, and 6 li, plus a regular tax of 1 yuan, 3 jiao, 4 fen, and 4 li, and a stamp tax of 7 jiao. There are many other small, difficult-to-donate expenses along the way, which are all unwarranted demands. When the goods arrive in Shanghai, a special tax of seven provinces must be paid, at 14 yuan per dan. If the goods are transshipped, a transshipment tax of 2 yuan, 4 jiao, and 4 fen per dan must be paid. In total, the tax per dan is over 40 yuan, while the cost of Western tobacco itself is only about 40 yuan per dan. Therefore, many of our businesses cannot afford the burden and are losing money. Those with slightly less financial resources have successively become insolvent and closed down. In recent years, the number of formal tobacco companies has decreased from twelve to only five. Although our industry is a trading merchant, it helps tobacco farmers in the producing areas, tobacco merchants in the sales areas, and tobacco workers in the processing and manufacturing areas. If our industry collapses, hundreds of thousands of tobacco farmers, tobacco workers, and merchants who depend on it for a living will perish together. At present, our industry is in dire straits. If the harsh and miscellaneous taxes along the way can be abolished and the government's tax system can be improved, our industry will still have a glimmer of hope. For this reason, we went to Beijing to petition at the Fifth General Assembly last May, requesting the government to protect industry and explicitly abolish all harsh and miscellaneous taxes on Western tobacco, and requesting the government to change the Western tobacco tax from a special tax system to a unified tax, allowing only one production tax to be collected, which would allow free sales throughout the country. However, almost a year has passed, and there has been no news. We do not know what the government's intentions are and are deeply confused. Now that your esteemed association is convening a representative assembly, our industry hereby submits this case, requesting all representatives of the assembly to unanimously resolve to forward it to the Ministry of Finance and immediately investigate the case, clearly ordering the provincial governments through which it passes to abolish the various harsh and miscellaneous taxes on Western tobacco, and at the same time change the special tax to a unified tax, to protect industry and relieve the difficulties of merchants. When the meeting arrived, it was submitted to the 7th Members' General Assembly of the affiliated association on the 20th of this month and passed, and handed over to the Executive Committee for handling. It is found that the amount of taxes and fees collected from the transportation of the industry's Western tobacco from the producing area to Shanghai, passing through various provinces, the number of items and the amount of fees, exceeds the cost, which is truly astonishing. In the face of the government's long-standing ban on lijin and similar harsh and miscellaneous taxes, the provinces still make their own decisions to exploit merchants, not only destroying the national tax discipline but also causing the industry's last chance of survival to perish. The industry's request to abolish the harsh and miscellaneous taxes in various provinces and change the special tax to a unified tax, allowing passage throughout the country after collecting one production tax, is based on the government's tax revenue and the relief of the industry's difficulties. It is appropriate to submit a petition to your esteemed department to quickly investigate the case and send it to the provincial governments, abolish the various harsh and miscellaneous taxes on Western tobacco, and devise a unified tax collection method to protect industry and commerce for public convenience."

City Chamber of Commerce Announces to All Industries that Merchants Should Restore Inherent Morality

Genuine Goods, Fair Prices, and Trustworthy Commerce – There is No Other Proper Way

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday announced to all industry associations, "We hereby inform you that when the Chamber of Commerce held its Seventh Members' Representative Assembly, the Petroleum Industry Trade Association proposed that we urge all industries to respect morality, eliminate false advertising, and self-destructive competition to preserve personal integrity and consolidate the commercial foundation. It stated, 'In recent times, commercial morality has become increasingly decadent. Most industries are engaged in scheming, vying to be strange and novel, and diligently engaged in false advertising, which leads to jealousy and mutual attacks among peers. As a result, they work hard but achieve little, which is tantamount to self-harm. Not only are they unable to attract general customers, but they also leave a bad impression in the minds of customers. Thinking of this, we can't help but feel sad. It must be known that commercial competition should use reasonable scientific methods, and merely lowering prices cannot be effective. Now that various industries have industry organizations, they should take the interests of the industry as a whole as their basis, and they must not harbor small personal prejudices and take private interests as their starting point. We dare to ask your association to urge all industries to strictly implement commercial morality, refrain from false advertising, and especially eliminate price competition that is close to self-harm. Then, the commercial future will rely on it.' It is found that the inherent commercial morality of our country is genuine goods, fair prices, and trustworthy commerce. Indeed, if we want to seek the development of individual businesses, there is no other proper way other than these eight characters. Since the opening of trade, foreign merchants have also praised Chinese merchants for having the virtues of truthfulness and trustworthiness and are happy to trade with them. The commercial prosperity of various trading ports in the past was due to this. Recently, due to the global economic downturn, the organization of the business itself may not be sound, resulting in selfishness and the discovery of various bad habits such as false advertising and jealousy among peers, which is the opposite of the inherent virtues mentioned above. Seeking commercial development in this way is a far cry. We hereby send a special letter to inform you, hoping that you will check and encourage yourselves in the same industry, restore the inherent morality of merchants, and promote prosperity, which is deeply hoped for."

Shipping, Shipbuilding, and Insurance Industries Jointly Operate a Cooperative Dockyard Plan

Hoping to Turn the Linked Business into a Three-in-One

The plan for the joint operation of a cooperative dockyard by the shipping, shipbuilding, and insurance industries has been passed by the General Assembly of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Trade Association and handed over to the Executive Committee for handling. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency learned the facts, reasons, and methods yesterday. The original text is as follows:

Facts and Reasons: (A) Facts and Reasons: Ship repair is very important. Although Shanghai is the center of private shipping, there are still few suitable private docks. If both supply and demand parties want to seek safety, economy, and convenience, it is necessary to jointly operate a "cooperative dockyard." In the shipping industry, all ships registered in Shanghai have always experienced difficulties and losses in regular annual repairs and temporary emergency repairs due to the lack of economical and convenient docks. If the factory can openly and universally solicit Shanghai shipowners to invest in the "cooperative dockyard," there will definitely be a response. The factory can take shareholder ship repair as its basic business, and it is estimated that there are about 100 ships of various sizes. Each ship repair costs about 5,000 yuan, so the annual repair fee of about 500,000 yuan can be obtained without soliciting shares. According to the investment and repair components, the distribution of profits will surely make everyone happy. In terms of the shipyard, an investigation of past facts shows that the factory lacks a dock and improvises, and may have suffered significant losses in terms of engineering and economy. For the sake of rational operation in the future, it is necessary to add a suitable dock to meet the reality and plan for development. Considering that the cost of the dock is huge, the factory is unable to complete it quickly, so it is possible to discuss with the parties in need to cooperate in the operation. (Geng San has repeatedly suggested to most shipowners and the Ship Insurance Federation and has received approval). In terms of the ship insurance industry, since the Shanghai Ship Federation was formed, it has been operating in cooperation, and its business has become increasingly developed. However, it is very difficult to inspect and repair due to the lack of a suitable dock. If the Shanghai private shipyard with technical reputation is consulted to operate a "standard" "cooperative dockyard" (accurate and economical), it can obtain the support of the Federation. It is hoped that all ships insured by the Federation will be limited to the "cooperative dockyard" and further attempts can be made. The Federation can also invest in the "cooperative dockyard" and can distribute profits according to the rules. The above four facts and reasons can be said to be an effective cooperation of the linked business and the three-in-one. The time has come, so do not let it pass by.

Specific Measures: (B) Methods: The Association will form a Preparatory Committee for Investment in the "Cooperative Dockyard" to first consult with a suitable Shanghai private shipyard. If it approves the principle, it will ask the factory to quickly draw up, the budget for the dock construction, the business estimate for the dock, the articles of association for soliciting shares in the "cooperative dockyard," the organization law for the "cooperative dockyard," the business, management, engineering, accounting, and various regulations for the "cooperative dockyard," the profit distribution regulations for the "cooperative dockyard" (must refer to cooperative principles and cooperative regulations), prepare the foundation for the dock, or find a way to purchase an existing suitable dock and renovate it for convenience. For the convenience of shipowners' investment, the Association should consult with appropriate business comrades and seriously suggest to the Shanghai banking group or the insurance industry to open a ship mortgage as a fund for shipowners to invest in the dock. The mortgage conditions can be strictly stipulated, because if the shipbuilding industry and the national shipping industry can be carried forward, then its development in financial insurance and production industry will also be like a shadow, and it can be guaranteed. The shipyard itself, in addition to its original business capital, should prepare one-third or one-half of the funds for the "cooperative dockyard." The shipyard should preferably consult with the banking group to do the "cooperative dockyard" mortgage. If it can be mortgaged by 50%, then the cooperative investor will be more likely to succeed (proposed by Wang Gengsan, representative of Tianjin Shipping Company).

Child Injured by Shanghai-Taizhou Bus

Transporting Opium in Linen Cloth? Trafficking from Sichuan Post Office to Shanghai for Sale, Police Investigation Results in Arrests

Recently, Liu Lixian, a native of Sichuan, 34 years old, rented a spare room at No. 218 Baker Road and falsely established the Fuyu Yong brand, pretending to sell Xia coarse cloth as a business. However, upon actual examination, it was found to be a secret drug trafficking organization. All morphine raw materials were transported from Sichuan to Shanghai, mixed in the Xia cloth. The center of each roll of Xia cloth was hollowed out and filled with morphine, so that the appearance could not be detected. It was sent to Shanghai by mail and sold for profit. However, due to the secrecy of the matter, Wang Chengying, Zhu Shuling, and Qian Xiaoting, detectives of the Anti-Narcotics Department, discovered the secret. They reported to the First Special Court the day before and signed a search warrant. At 10:15 p.m., they secretly went to No. 218 Baker Road and arrested Zheng Qianxiu, Liu Lixian, and Liu's concubine, Huang Yueying, all three natives of Shaoxing. They seized 52 rolls of Xia cloth, of which 26 rolls each contained a package of morphine, each package weighing nine taels, totaling fourteen pounds and ten taels, as well as opium smoking paraphernalia. Then, according to Liu's confession, they went to No. 12, Lane 396, Gongguanma Road in the French Concession to arrest the same party, Zeng Nansheng (i.e., Zeng Yongsheng), a native of Hubei. Zeng had gone out and did not return home until after 1:00 a.m. yesterday, when they arrested him. They found 15 taels of raw morphine material in the sofa cushion and one roll of similarly hollowed-out Xia cloth. They were taken to the Xinzha Patrol Room separately and detained. Yesterday morning, Zhang Tianyin, a patrol room lawyer, sent them to Criminal Division 8 of the First Special Court and prosecuted them for the crime of selling opium substitutes according to Article 257, Section 2 of the Criminal Law. He also stated the case, saying that the patrol room still needed to arrest accomplices in this case, so he requested a postponement, etc. Then, he presented the Xia cloth morphine to the court. Questioning Liu Lixian, he confessed that he had been selling morphine for three months. However, all the Xia cloth was sent from Sichuan to Shanghai by mail. Zheng Qianxiu was my fellow villager. He came to Shanghai not long ago and initially went to Huiji New Hotel, but recently began to live on the third floor of my house. All the Xia cloth sent from Sichuan to Shanghai was piled up on the third floor, etc. Zheng Qianxiu confessed that he was temporarily living in Liu's house and did not know about the sale. Huang Yueying confessed that she had been acquainted with Liu for a short time and did not know about the drug trafficking either. Zeng Nansheng confessed that he sold and peddled drugs for Liu, starting on the 16th of this month. He only earned commissions and sold more than one hundred taels of morphine in total, with a selling price of seven yuan per tael, etc. Judge Huang Risheng ruled that the case would be postponed to July 3 for further interrogation. Zheng Qianxiu and Huang Yueying were released on bail of 2,000 yuan. Zheng and Zeng were returned to the patrol room for detention.

Regarding the price increase issue, evidence should be collected to verify whether the company's income exceeds 10% in order to file a negotiation, etc. Accordingly, in addition to notifying users to quickly report the new price payment bills and the situation of inaccurate accounting and exceeding the number of times to the Special District Telephone Problem Committee in the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce in Tianhougong Bridge, the number so far is small and cannot verify whether the company's income exceeds 10%. Therefore, according to the Shanghai Telephone Company's price increase law passed by the Public Works Department Board of Directors, the attached conditions, Section 2, "According to the contract signed between the company and the Public Works Department, assuming that the income exceeds one point, the company should waive one-half of the excess amount," Section 3, "All expenses of the company should be reduced as much as possible," and Section 4, "If the future income exceeds one point, the Public Works Department should immediately convene a board of directors meeting to re-discuss reducing telephone charges," etc., in order to facilitate the collection of user documents, all industry associations are requested to notify their members to send the telephone bills to the Chamber of Commerce so that a letter can be sent to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association to request the Public Works Department Board of Directors to re-negotiate and reduce telephone charges, etc. Accordingly, we hereby request that you follow the instructions.

User Report

The Special District Telephone Problem Committee received a letter from the Children's Bookstore on Sima Road yesterday, saying that the "91923" telephone installed in our store, in addition to the fixed price in the previous month, if we add the charge for Huajie telephones according to regulations at nine cents each time, the monthly calculation only requires about nineteen yuan, and at most it is only sixteen or seventeen yuan. This time, after the company changed the new regulations, the monthly telephone bill suddenly increased to thirty yuan and some odd cents. It was found that our store counted a total of 485 calls from February 21 to April 20 this year, excluding the 150 calls that should be made within the rules, exceeding 335 times. According to the company's new single three cents each time, it is 10.005 yuan, plus the fixed fee of 10 yuan, it is only 20 yuan and odd cents. However, the company's bill from March 17 to April 16 shows 636 excess calls, a difference of 301 calls. Also, from April 22 to May 20, the count was 361 calls, excluding the number of calls that should be made, exceeding 211 times, while the company's bill from April 17 to September 16 shows 522 excess calls, a difference of 311 calls. Moreover, our store records each telephone call on a nameplate. We questioned the company directly last month. The company was nothing more than covering up with evasive words, only using the counting meter installed in the company as proof. At that time, we asked them to also install a counting meter on our store's telephone to verify, but the company did not give a clear answer, which is very sad. If this continues, the losses will be countless. Therefore, we enclose two copies of the new price payment bill and request that you uphold justice and negotiate according to reason, etc.

Mirage Discovered Outside Wusong Estuary Yesterday Afternoon

Buildings and Pavilions Clearly Discernible, Figures Coming and Going Faintly Visible

A mirage phenomenon was discovered near the Gaoqiao coast outside the Wusong Estuary at about 1:30 p.m. yesterday. At that time, majestic and magnificent architectural giant shadows suddenly appeared in the vast ocean, towering into the clouds. Due to the dazzling sunlight, the buildings were in five colors, purple, gold, etc. Among them, buildings and pavilions, carved beams, were clearly discernible, and figures coming and going were faintly visible. For a time, many villagers gathered to watch. However, because it was very temporary and disappeared in a few minutes, those who arrived later were unable to fully enjoy the spectacle and felt deeply regretful, it is said.

Re-equipping of Flatbed Cart Wheels Comes to a Satisfactory End

Previous Proposal Indefinitely Postponed

Regarding the re-equipping of flatbed cart wheels in the Public Concession, the Flatbed Cart Industry Mutual Aid Association repeatedly petitioned the Public Works Department to temporarily exempt them from re-equipping. Recently, the department's security committee convened a meeting to discuss it. As a result, the previous proposal that all carts should be equipped with angle iron wheels at least 3.5 inches wide or solid rubber tires at least 1 inch wide starting on July 1 of the Japanese year was deemed sufficient to increase the burden on cart merchants and difficult to implement under the current situation. It was resolved to petition the Board of Directors to indefinitely postpone the previous proposal, and the current regulations for flatbed carts and other vehicles will also not be revised for the time being. It is also heard that the Public Works Department Board of Directors, when holding a regular meeting yesterday, had approved the proposal of the Security Committee. Therefore, the re-equipping of flatbed cart wheels has come to a satisfactory end.

Homeless People in the Xiqin Institute Beat a Patrolman to Death, Interrogation

Gao Fuxiang, Pan Qianhe Shou, Hong Jianfu, etc., homeless people taken in by the homeless people's Xiqin Institute in Caohe, and Yao Benren, Gao Yongling, Wu Ruilin, etc., who were at large, because of digging a hole and escaping resistance to arrest, designed to beat Patrolman Lu Yecai to death. At that time, Gao Fuxiang, Pan Heshou, and Hong Jianfu were arrested, and Yao Benren, Gao Yongling, Wu Ruilin, etc., fled. They were sent to the local court for investigation and were prosecuted for murder. Yesterday, Judge Zhao Yongzhou held a court hearing. Gao Fuxiang confessed that he was 22 years old, a local, living at No. 177 Tangjiawan, and worked in a rice shop. The official asked why he was sent to the Homeless People's Xiqin Institute. He replied that he was addicted to gambling and was sent to the Public Security Bureau by his father on December 5 last year and transferred to the Xiqin Institute. The official asked why he wanted to kill Patrolman Lu Yecai. He replied that it was not his idea, it was Tao Benren and Wu Ruilin who came up with the idea. On February 3, because they wanted to dig a hole and escape, Wu Ruilin suggested tying up Lu Yecai. Therefore, Yao Benren covered Lu's head with a blanket, and Lu shouted. Gao Yongling started to beat him, and Hong Jianfu was guarding the door. Because Lu kept shouting, we were afraid of making noise and not following, so Wu Ruilin and I each held iron rods and files to beat him. After we left, he was not dead yet. The official asked what Pan Heshou was doing at that time. He replied that he was helping Yao Benren cover Lu's head. The official asked how many times he hit him. He replied that he hit him once, and Wu Ruilin hit him three times. The official asked why they wanted to escape. He replied that it was because the institute was so painful that they were beaten if they were not careful. The official asked if they would pay for killing someone with their lives. He replied that he had no choice. At this point, Pan Heshou confessed that he was 22 years old and a native of Taiyu. Because of wandering and gambling, his father, Pan Donggen, sent him to the Xiqin Institute in May last year. The official asked that his father sent him because he meant well. Why did he escape? He replied, yes, I did not come up with the idea. At that time, when they discussed escaping, I said that if things did not work out, they would be beaten. So I was advising them, but they would not listen. At that time, because it was difficult to open the hole for a while, Hong Jianfu pretended to be sick and slept on the bed, covering it with a quilt. Then Patrolman Lu Yecai came to check on them, and they beat him. After they left, I followed them out and was arrested, etc. Hong Jianfu, 18 years old, from Cixi, parents died, married, has a sister and a brother, studying in Annam, came to Shanghai for only more than ten days, living at No. 469 Jiangxi Road. Because he had no job, he voluntarily went to the institute to learn skills and did mechanical work on April 5 of the noon year. I did not dare to oppose what they did, nor did I dare to report it. I did not know the roads in Shanghai, and I had no money, so I did not conspire with them, etc. According to Patrolman Sun Jinhai and Liu Shangzhi of the institute, Lu Yecai was injured on February 3 and died the next day. The official ruled that the case would be investigated and interrogated again, and the defendants were returned to custody.

Liu Huizhi, Accused of Embezzlement and Breach of Trust, Continued Trial Yesterday

Plaintiff Asks the Judge to Detain Liu Because the Case is Serious

Liu Huizhi, chairman and general manager of the Zhong 　 Industrial Bank, a native of Anhui, 　was sued by shareholders Xiang Jiewan, Weng Pengnian, Zhu Junping, Yan Jiquan, Yan Shuyi, and Chen, a lawyer, for embezzling the letter of credit in the First Special District Court, reaching seven articles. Then, He and others added a lawsuit against Li Jizhi, the current managing director of the Yihang Bank, and listed him as a joint defendant. The court once summoned him, but because the defendant did not arrive,　 ordered a rescheduling of the trial. All the details have been reported in the 16th edition of this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Tan of 　 Criminal Division 8 continued the trial. Liu Huizhi arrived in court with his defense lawyer, and Li Jizhi did not arrive, but entrusted a lawyer to represent him. Liu's lawyer then raised a procedural issue, saying that Zhang Chongfu, a shareholder of the former China Industrial Bank, loved His Honor's accusations against Liu. Five of the facts he sued were completely identical to those sued in this case. After His Honor believed that it should first be determined whether there was a right to sue under civil law, I ruled to suspend the trial. Now that the civil case has not been determined, according to law, the five articles of the same case, since they belong to the same facts and the same defendant, should also be suspended, etc. The plaintiff argued that because there were two cases and the plaintiffs were not the same, they were not bound by the previous ruling. The lawyers on both sides had a long and fierce debate on this issue based on legal precedents. Judge Tan ruled that whether or not to suspend the trial on these five items should be determined by the court separately, and the remaining items still needed to collect evidence, so he ruled to reschedule the trial and wait for further summons. The plaintiff's lawyer then stated that on the surface, the amount of Liu Huizhi's embezzlement was four or five million, but in reality, it was more than tens of millions. Therefore, the circumstances of the case were serious, and he requested that the defendant be detained. Judge Tan then asked Liu if he could be present every time he was summoned in the future. Liu said he would definitely be able to appear in court. The court then ruled that the trial should be suspended for paragraphs one to five as filed by the plaintiff, and the remaining paragraphs should be suspended for further investigation, and then adjourned to await further summons.

A Thief Carelessly Touched the Back Door Lock; Remaining Thieves Panicked and Jumped Out of the Building

All Were Arrested Due to Injuries

The Victim Personally Testified in Court

The thieves, Zhang Xiaodi from Jiaxing, Wang Laowu and Zhong Jinsheng from Suzhou, and Shen Zhangsheng (at large), at 11:20 PM, carried axes to the Hu Qing Tobacco and Paper Shop at No. 245 Han Road. They broke in through the back door, threatened to silence the occupants with axes, and robbed approximately thirty yuan in banknotes and coins. Shen, the first thief to flee through the back door, inadvertently triggered the spring lock, causing panic among the other three thieves. Fearing that the police would arrive from the front to arrest them, they hastily went upstairs and jumped from the曬tai, attempting to escape. Zhang Xiaodi fell and injured his head, fainting on the spot. Zhong Jinsheng suffered a jaw injury and hid in a narrow alley in Huasheng Road’s Xieyu Lane. Wang Laowu sustained a minor waist injury and barely managed to return home to No. 76 Yangzhou Road. At that time, the Yulin Road police station received a report and dispatched Detective Li Hongsheng and other Western detectives to investigate. Near the shop's back door, they found Zhang Xiaodi lying on the ground, attempting to get up and leave. He was immediately arrested and searched, revealing sixteen yuan and six jiao in stolen coins. Questioning him revealed that his accomplices were hiding at No. 76 Yangzhou Road, where Wang was also arrested. Zhong was later apprehended in Xieyu Lane on Huasheng Road, and one yuan and nine jiao in stolen coins were found on him. An axe was also recovered from the shop's 曬tai. All were taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Special First Court. Zhang Shizhu, the lawyer from the Public Works Department, detailed the events and requested an extension for investigation. Hu Qingping, the shop owner, and Detective Li testified about the incident, presenting the axe and stolen coins as evidence. Judge Jiang Shuzi questioned the three defendants, ordering them to be remanded in custody for further review.

Xiang Stage Smashed

Three Policemen Beaten; Spectators Caught in the Crossfire

Several people went to watch a play at the Xiang Stage at No. 2 Tianshi Road, Zhabei, during the Dragon Boat Festival. A minor disagreement with the tea servers arose, and the stage manager, Qu Hongxi, apologized to resolve the matter. Unexpectedly, around 8 PM last night, the stage was suddenly attacked. A spectator in the pool seats, wearing yellow shorts and a black long衫, initiated the questioning of why the fans were not turned on. While speaking, he proceeded to dismantle the electric fans. The stage staff and tea servers naturally stepped forward to stop him and negotiate, but before words could be exchanged, a brawl erupted. Other spectators, fearing for their safety, scrambled to escape, creating a chaotic and noisy scene. The performance on stage was also halted. The brawlers, seeing the play had stopped, seized the opportunity to rush onto the stage and tear down the scenery. At that moment, Wu Changhong, the stage's security guard, realizing the situation was beyond control, frantically blew the警笛for help and held the iron gate to prevent the rioters from escaping. Police officer No. 26, patrolling from the Linping Road police station, and the police at the Tianbing Road post, arrived first. As they prepared to enter and suppress the riot, the perpetrators charged out of the venue, mistaking the officers for their targets. Without inquiry, they attacked the three officers with wooden sticks and槍柄, injuring all three. By the time a large contingent of police from the Linping Road police station arrived, the rioters had fled without a trace. The injured officers and spectators/stage employees Wang Hanzhang, Liu Guanchang, Zhong Wenlong, Huang Shifu, Zhu Chunjiang, and Wang Zhangshi were immediately transported to Tongren Hospital. Another seven or eight people with minor injuries went home to treat themselves. An investigation into the damage and the whereabouts of the perpetrators was launched to bring them to justice. The losses sustained by the Xiang Stage were substantial, as the equipment, decor, and scenery had all been destroyed.

Publication of "A Practical Discussion of Ancient Coins"

This book is written by Mr. Ding Fubao. It considers ancient coins as a branch of epigraphy and discusses six practical benefits of studying them: 1) It can examine the merits and demerits of monetary systems throughout history; 2) It can examine ancient weights and measures; 3) It can increase the interest in reading books; 4) It can correct errors in various books; 5) It can correct some ancient rare characters; 6) It can serve as a pastime for the elderly. The book elaborates on these six points, quoting extensively and accurately. It also includes many rubbings of famous ancient coins, reproduced with exceptional clarity, making the illustrations as vivid as seeing the actual coins. It is truly an interesting book for studying ancient coins and a guide for beginners. The publisher is the Shanghai Meibaige Road No. 204 Medical Bookstore. Each copy sells for one yuan. A summary of the book on ancient coin industry will be sent upon request.

Vienna Hosts Press Conference for News Reporters: The Vienna Garden Ballroom at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Dahua Road, in addition to renovating the existing garden part for this summer, has added a viewing fish pond. It purchased at military prices various glass fish produced in South America, with a variety of colors, which is sufficient. When reflected in the lights, the bones in the fish's abdomen can be seen, which is truly a spectacle. These glass fish are kept in a huge glass tank, which stands high in the dance floor. While dancing, people can freely view the various postures of the fish. The interior of the ballroom has been specially equipped with the latest type of cold air system by the Sita Company. This equipment is still a novel concept at sea. It uses scientific methods to reduce the heat in the room and provide fresh air. When dancing, people only feel a cool breeze, rising from the ground. Chen Zhanxiong, the manager of the garden, wanted to promote all the equipment in the garden and improve social dance, so he specially hosted a banquet for reporters from various newspapers in the city at 7:00 PM yesterday afternoon. During the banquet, he also explained the meaning of social dance, briefly explaining that dancing is a type of exercise and is also a necessary piece of knowledge in social settings. The trend of dancing in our country is less than ten years old, but it has gradually developed this year. Some people attack dancing as harmful to morals, but dancing itself is not harmful. Only those who use the name of dancing to do bad things should be avoided. Therefore, those who love dancing should recognize the content and organization of the ballroom. Anything that damages our reputation and spirit should be avoided, so that we can benefit from dancing.

Shanghai's Oil Extraction Industry

— Edited by China Credit

(Summary of Shanghai Industry and Commerce 29)

2. Raw Materials

Shanghai's oil extraction industry is quite similar to the flour industry, that is, the flour industry often stops business due to a decrease or severance in the supply of wheat. The oil extraction industry also often cannot continue production due to a lack of various plant seeds, so the supply of raw materials is closely related to the future of the industry. The main products of Shanghai's oil extraction plants are cottonseed oil, soybean oil, vegetable oil, and rapeseed oil. Now, the supply of raw materials will be analyzed below:

1. Cottonseed: The raw material for cottonseed oil is cottonseed, which is attached to the cotton boll. According to its color, it is divided into two types: green, black, and white. The oil quality of green is the best. According to its type, there are differences between American cotton, Indian cotton, and Egyptian cotton, etc. The Egyptian cottonseed has the most oil, about 16%. As for the cottonseed needed in this city, there are three sources: one is the cotton-growing areas of Sichuan, Hunan, Hubei, and Shaanxi, with an annual amount of more than 2 million loads; the second is the Shaoxing and Yuyao area of Zhejiang, with an annual amount of only 200,000 loads; and the third is the newly reclaimed cotton area north and south of the Yangtze River in Jiangsu, with an annual amount of 800,000 loads. Hebei and Shandong were originally vast cotton-producing areas, second only to the Northwest, but because the Japanese rose up to monopolize them, they are almost useless to my country's oil extraction industry. In addition to competing for our country's raw materials, it also has the incidental effect of monopolizing our country's cottonseed, which will inevitably hinder our country's or this city's oil extraction industry no less than the cotton textile industry, which is neglected by Chinese people and should be given more attention.

2. Soybeans: The raw material for soybean oil is soybeans. There are many types of soybeans, which can be roughly divided into four types: yellow soybeans, Jinyuan, Bai Mei, and Hei Qi. Yellow soybeans are the most common soybeans, with the largest yield, and are also the main raw material for soybean oil. Jinyuan is named for its yellow color and round shape, and contains a lot of oil. Bai Mei is also known as Bai Ban or Da Bai Mei. Hei Qi is also known as Hei Fu, with a white tendon on one abdomen and a dark brown tendon on the other. The oil content is more than Jinyuan. My country is the country with the most abundant soybean production, such as the four provinces of Hubei, Hunan, Anhui, and Jiangsu in the Yangtze River Basin, and the three provinces of Henan, Shandong, and Shanxi in the Yellow River Basin, all of which produce soybeans. However, the soybeans produced in the Northeast are the most abundant. In addition to a part of the soybeans needed in this city being supplied by Jiangsu Province, the rest are purchased from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and the Jinpu area.

3. Peanuts: Vegetable oil is peanut oil, and its raw material is peanuts without shells. The quality is determined by the number of grains contained in each ounce. Generally, the best is 28 grains per ounce, and the worst is 40 or 50 grains per ounce. The former can extract 60 catties of oil per load, and the latter can extract 30 catties of oil per load. Ordinary peanuts can extract 50 catties of oil. The climate and soil of each province in my country are generally suitable for cultivating peanuts, so peanut production is almost all over the country. However, Shandong produces the most, with an annual output of more than 170 million loads. Hunan and Fujian provinces produce the least, about 1 million loads per year. Most of the peanuts needed in this city are traded in Qingdao and Xuzhou.

4. Rapeseed: Rapeseed is the raw material for rapeseed oil. The vegetables that produce the rapeseed are mainly rapeseed, which is called rapeseed by the local people. Now, the types and the amount of oil contained in each type when dried are listed as follows:

The important producing areas of rapeseed are the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, and the oil in Jin, Lu, and Ji is sold inland, replacing the position of soybean oil as fuel, so soybean oil in the inland is currently only used for cooking, so most of the rapeseed is also imported into this city from the countryside.

In addition, coconut oil has been produced in this city in recent years, and it is heard that under the support of the business department, a tung oil factory may appear soon, so we cannot ignore the two raw materials, coconut and tung seeds. In addition, in addition to the cottonseed being mainly purchased from various yarn factories in this city, the remaining oil extraction raw materials mentioned above are all purchased by the factory by sending personnel to the inland. Some inland merchants also sell to oil factories in this city, and the miscellaneous grain stores in this city often operate in the operation of these raw materials. (To be continued)

Treatment of Chronic Gonorrhea

Once gonorrhea becomes chronic, complications arise endlessly. The reason why chronic gonorrhea is difficult to cure lies in this. Generally, at the onset of gonorrhea, the lesions are mostly located in the anterior part of the urethra. At this time, the gonococcal toxins have not yet established a base, making it easiest to expel them. This is because the tissue of the anterior urethra is very simple, and it is not easy for gonococci to hide. Once it becomes chronic, the gonococci move from the anterior urethra to the posterior urethra and then invade the testicles, vas deferens, seminal vesicles, and paraurethral ducts.

The most obvious symptom of chronic gonorrhea is the absence of severe pain during the acute stage. Sometimes it is subtle or nonexistent, with only one or two drops of leukorrhea. Often, the external symptoms are almost nonexistent, and it only flares up after being stimulated. If the patient's urine is examined under a microscope, many gonococci will be found in the urine. Because these bacteria are always attached to the mucous membrane of the urethra, they are often discharged during urination and ejaculation, making it very easy to infect the opposite sex.

Special methods must be used to treat this type of chronic gonorrhea. In my clinical practice, I always use anti-gonococcal serum and X-rays to eliminate gonococci, and supplement them with electrotherapy and effective oral medications for gonorrhea, all of which can be cured in the shortest possible time. This is because these treatments adopt an encirclement policy, making it impossible for gonococci to escape. As for women suffering from gonococcal leukorrhea, effective oral medications for gonorrhea can be taken internally, and vaginal tablets can be used externally, which can also achieve a radical cure in a short period.

Venue for the Next Olympic Games Mr. Bailaila expresses his views. He doesn't want to express his opinion alone because of his duty. A three-way race often makes it easier to see each other's strengths and weaknesses

Paris, June 24 (Havas) - Count Bailaila, Chairman of the International Olympic Committee, recently stated to a reporter from this agency, "The venue for the 12th Olympic Games in 1940 is being contested by the United Kingdom, Japan, and Finland. As Chairman of the International Olympic Committee, it is not convenient for me to express my opinion alone and hastily consider which country is more suitable. I have just returned from the capital of Finland and found that the country has all the conditions to host the next Games. Now the United Kingdom has also made the same request, so we should discuss it carefully. However, this move by the United Kingdom has not reduced Japan's chances of hosting the next Games, because, according to common sense, it is easier to see each other's strengths and weaknesses when there are three parties competing than when there are only two parties."

Olympics - An Explanation of Diving Competitions and Illustrations of Various Dives (1)

— Qian Yidong

A Few Words

The English word "Diving" is often translated by our countrymen as "entering the water" (as seen in the current swimming rules). Upon careful consideration, this seems inappropriate. It would be better to call it "leaping into the water" (躍水). The character "躍" (yue) implies the meaning of a fish leaping. From a specialized perspective, the core of diving truly lies in the moment of leaping and being in the air, not in the instant of entering the water. Although entering the water is also within the scope of diving, its study is subtle. Therefore, the emphasis should be on "leaping" (躍) rather than "entering" (入). Regarding diving itself, it is essential for divers to strive for height in their jumps. Once they submerge into the water, the dive is complete. Diving is a specialized skill in swimming. However, our country's athletes have not shown widespread interest and training in it. Although there are many reasons for this, a significant one is that it is only listed as a demonstration event in the National Games. Therefore, it should be changed to a formal championship event in the future (please refer to my article "Points for Improvement in Organizing Sports Meets," published in the Diligent Sports Monthly, Volume 3, Issue 7). Furthermore, the Olympic diving events and rules should be adopted. This is the motivation for roughly translating this article.

The most significant difficulty at present is the lack of diving terminology. In this article, I have tried my best to use existing names for various dives, but many are newly created. There are bound to be many inappropriate aspects. I hope that fellow members of the sports community will correct them. The international diving rules and illustrations are detailed below.

General Rules

1. All diving competitions organized in international sports events must follow the rules of the International Amateur Swimming Federation.

2. The springboards, platforms, and all diving equipment must comply with the current rules.

3. All diving equipment must be prepared at least eight days before the competition for the use of participating athletes.

4. The order of divers must be determined by drawing lots.

5. The drawing of lots must be conducted publicly. The time and location of the drawing must be stated in the competition notice.

6. If necessary, athletes may be divided into groups. The number of athletes in each group shall be determined by the review committee. The results of all groups must be reviewed to determine the final ranking. The entire competition must be completed within one day.

7. Before each dive, the chief judge must announce the athlete's name and the dive they intend to perform in advance.

8. Athletes should be given sufficient time to prepare and execute their dives.

9. Only dives listed in the table in these rules may be performed.

10. Each competition must include a certain number of required dives and optional dives.

11. Each athlete must complete the official form for their optional dives (either typed or handwritten), and submit a copy at least one week before the competition. The form must include:

(A) The category and number of the dive.

(B) The name of the dive and the starting method (running or standing).

(C) The height of the springboard or platform.

(D) The degree of difficulty (difficulty).

12. Required dives must not be repeated in the optional dives. All dives with the same number are considered the same dive.

13. Athletes must sign the optional dive list. No changes may be made after the designated time. Each athlete is fully responsible for the accuracy of the information on the list.

14. Athletes who do not submit the list within the designated time will not be allowed to participate in the competition.

15. If the information on the list does not comply with the rules, the chief judge must decide before the competition whether to order corrections, make further adjustments, or refuse the athlete's participation.

16. All dives must be performed by the athlete themselves, without any assistance from others.

Zhejiang Education and Culture Funding Increased by 500,000 Compared to Last Year

The Zhejiang Province's estimated budget for education and culture in the 25th year of the Republic (1936) has been compiled and sent to the Finance Department for compilation and submission to the Provincial Government meeting on the 26th for discussion. The figures have been moderately increased compared to the previous year. The reasons for this increase are the addition of 17 classes in senior and junior high schools, an increase in the food and allowance subsidies for normal school students, an increase in scholarships and free/publicly funded student quotas, and the addition of 280,000 yuan for compulsory education expenses, a doubling of the previous amount. The total expenditure is 3,019,577 yuan, an increase of 498,733 yuan compared to the 2,520,844 yuan listed in the previous year.

Fujian Province Reorganizing Higher Education - University Departments Defined to Avoid Duplication - Suspension of Government-Funded Overseas Study and Scholarships/Subsidies for Self-Funded Study

(Xiamen Dispatch) The Fujian Provincial Government has decided to reorganize university education in the province starting from the autumn semester of the 25th year of the Republic (1936). Among the plans for reorganizing education in the province, the measures for reorganizing higher education involve reorganizing the colleges and departments established by various private universities and independent colleges. (A) Principles of Reorganization: To ensure that the departments established by each university and college are appropriate, without duplication or waste. To enable each university and college to focus on the development of a specific department, so that the level can be improved. To enable the establishment of important departments that have not yet been established. To enable each university and college to cooperate and form a comprehensive university. (B) Reorganization Measures: Xiamen University will establish three colleges: Arts, Sciences, Law, and Commerce. Each college will have the following departments: The College of Arts will have departments of Chinese Literature, History and Geography, and Education. The College of Sciences will have departments of Mathematics, Physics, Zoology, and Botany. The College of Law and Commerce will have departments of Commerce, Political Science, and Economics. Concord College will establish two departments: Arts and Sciences, with the following departments: The Arts department will have departments of Foreign Languages and Sociology. The Science department will have departments of Chemistry, Biology, and Physiology. Fujian College will be renamed Fujian Law College, the agriculture department will be abolished, and a law department will be established. The South China Women's College of Arts and Sciences will temporarily not divide into colleges, but will establish the following departments and specialized courses: The College of Arts and Sciences will have departments of Literature, Home Economics, and Music, as well as specialized courses in Physical Education, Home Economics, and Art. The Department of Education will convene a meeting of the presidents of various universities in July of this year to discuss how to implement the reorganization measures in phases, and to discuss matters of division of labor and cooperation at any time. The standards for the allocation of subsidies to private universities are as follows: (A) Xiamen University will receive a monthly subsidy of 4,500 yuan, specifically designated to subsidize the departments of Mathematics, Physics, and History and Geography. (B) Fujian College will receive a monthly subsidy of 1,000 yuan, with 60% designated for professors' salaries and 40% for purchasing books. The Provincial Government has also decided to suspend government-funded overseas study and scholarships/subsidies for self-funded overseas study starting from the 25th year of the Republic (1936), and to concentrate these funds on expanding and reorganizing education in the province. (June 25)

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education issued an order yesterday to secondary schools in the city, stating: According to the Ministry of Education's Instruction No. Jun Yi Yi Eighth Seven Nine Nine of June 20 of this year, the outline of secondary school special education stipulates that senior high schools and equivalent schools implement military management, and the military training uniform will be the student uniform. Soviet Union Plans to Reform Universities

(TASS, Moscow, June 24) The Council of People's Commissars and the Central Committee of the Communist Party have resolved to guide the reform of universities and specialized schools. The resolution, signed by Molotov and Stalin, has been published. The resolution states that the Stakhanovite movement has exposed the fact that the scientific education work of higher education institutions lags far behind its implementation. Therefore, it is necessary to revise curricula, textbooks, reference books, encyclopedias, and technical teaching materials to adapt them to the results of the Stakhanovite movement. Higher demands must be placed on higher education institutions to ensure that young people receive excellent training, political and general education, and can fully control the latest achievements in science, combining theory with practice and industrial experience with science.

The resolution stipulates that young people aged 17 to 35 who have completed full secondary education and passed the examination can enter higher education for free. The time for compulsory independent study courses under the guidance of professors will be reduced to increase students' independent research, and special libraries, laboratories, and science rooms will be established to facilitate independent research.

The resolution stipulates that technical specialized schools must hold meetings before the government examination committee. Industrial practice must occupy a fixed position in the entire curriculum. Students must engage in industrial practice in their special research departments. The best-equipped enterprises must provide opportunities for students of technical specialized schools to practice. The practice time in the last two years should account for more than 30%. The resolution stipulates a plan for improving the management of higher education, and a special clause forces supervisors to pay attention to students' physical fitness and health and guarantee them a good life.

Jiangsu Education Department Asks Schools to Pay Attention to Children's Health

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, in view of the fact that although primary schools pay great attention to children's mental training, there are still several points that contradict children's health and hygiene, which have a significant impact on children's development. Recently, it has been learned that primary schools encourage children to be diligent by ranking those who arrive at school first as an honor. While the intention is good, the method is not perfect. School-age children are full of competitive spirit, and often get up early before dawn, quickly eating breakfast, only to arrive first. After arriving at school, the time before class often reaches more than one hour. This reduces sleep time and wastes the early morning hours, which over time will significantly affect children's health. Therefore, a special order has been issued to the education bureaus of various counties to instruct schools to pay special attention and make corrections.

Finance - Rumors of Positive News, Gold Prices Still Stuck in a Range

Closing Prices Unchanged

Although London spot gold fell yesterday, major players were interested in buying, preventing the market from falling. Longs also liquidated at highs, resulting in a range-bound market. In the morning, overseas silver markets saw the pound rise and the dollar remain flat. Market talk suggested sellers below the listed price of .0625 after the close, leading to a weaker market sentiment. Silver forwards were unchanged or slightly higher by up to 1/100 of a penny. Exchange rates fluctuated. London spot gold fell 1.5 pence. The central bank's fixing was announced, with both the pound and the dollar unchanged. The customs gold unit narrowed by 0.02. The standard gold bar price was fixed lower at 1127.3 yuan. Over-the-counter pre-market trading opened at around 38.5 yuan. Fu Tai Heng Lai progressed and opened flat. Major players still entered the market after the opening, temporarily rebounding the price. However, due to longs taking the opportunity to sell, the overall trend remained range-bound. The HSBC fixing was announced, with both the pound and the dollar unchanged, resulting in further declines. The silver balancing tax was revealed to be up by 1.25 fen. There was some consolidation in the middle, but the overall trend remained weak due to continued selling by longs. The market trend consolidated at noon. In the afternoon, the market remained weak due to continued selling by longs. Later, rumors of positive news boosted market sentiment, gradually rebounding the price. Longs still sold at highs, resulting in a fairly stable result. Yesterday's swaps were quoted at 4 to 4.4 yuan by longs. The day's market conditions are recorded below.
