Commercial Finance Was So-So

This year's commercial sector, judging from its appearance, seems to have made progress, and some banks have jointly formed syndicates to provide loans to help rural areas and the silk and tea industries. However, it is still difficult to say what the actual situation is. As for commercial credit loans, they rely on actual strength these days. If a company's own ability is weak, it can't even take care of itself, how can it take care of others? Therefore, the situation of this year's semi-annual closing accounts is that 70-80% of the companies have no profit to speak of. For example, the closure of the Tongyi Trust Company was partly due to speculative failures, and partly due to years of losses and many bad debts at each closing, so the company could not operate smoothly. This kind of situation is worrying in every way. It is already fortunate not to lose money; wanting to make a profit is rare except for a few major banks. To say that the entire commercial sector is gradually showing signs of recovery is indeed what we hope for.

Securities August Public Bonds Debuted Yesterday, Market Still Unable to Rally

From Low to High: From High to Low: Quite Like a Parabola

Yesterday, the August futures of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange debuted, coinciding with renewed serious rumors from the Hunan border. The August futures opened fully in the first session, with market prices mostly matching the recent "small three yuan" after deducting interest. However, there was still no profit to be made from arbitrage, and the market remained sluggish. The situation concerning the Hunan border troops was precarious, with talk of increasing stakes. Rumors in the north had not subsided, and under such circumstances, it was not easy for the market to rise.

Throughout yesterday morning, selling pressure was strong, with Nos. 5, 35, and 47 being sold, and Nos. 11 and 54 being bought. August futures also opened across the board, with prices falling uniformly by three jiao to half a yuan. In the second session, the shorts covered strongly, but mostly by scattered retail investors. The rebound was strong, with Type D stocks surging by seven and a half jiao, and others rising by four or five jiao. In the afternoon session, the initial trades continued to strengthen, with Type E and D stocks continuing to rise by one to four jiao. When Type C stocks were being traded, rumors suddenly arrived, and selling orders from Nos. 4, 10, and 47 flooded in, causing Type C to immediately fall by two and a half jiao, Type B by as much as seven jiao, and Type A by about three jiao. The trend was immediately hit. When prices were high, people sold off, and when prices were low, people bought in, so market prices fluctuated widely.

Whether the front-line battles will erupt or if there is still room for maneuver is the crucial key to current market prices. Observing the weak closing prices in the afternoon, it is expected that new lows may be seen in the future. The market results, excluding the initial opening of August futures, showed that Type D stocks still rose by one jiao, while the rest fell slightly by five fen to one or two jiao. The trend was from low to high, then from high to low, showing a complete inability to rally. The total transaction volume was 915 lots, totaling 5,000 yuan. The results of the gains and losses are compared in the table on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan).

Shen Bao Literary Weekly

Old Notes from the Mountains

— Before Coming to Shanghai, Autumn 1935 —

Rosa! Your letter has stirred up the waves in my heart again. How can the tranquility of the mountains calm my heart?

"Being nurtured by nature cannot alleviate your illness. It will only deepen it!" R, this is your warning to me, and you know how touched I am by these words!

If I had come into contact with ph.'s works earlier, I would have mustered the courage to rush to Shanghai regardless, to plunge into the torrent of life. If I had seen [your letter] before coming here, I would have left this "high mountain" - why are you so playful? - to live in your "small room." But I have already come here to "avoid the autumn" - now is the time when those idle and wealthy city dwellers who came here to escape the summer are descending the mountain. My coming here has only made me feel the ancient city's "autumn wind, autumn rain, so deadly," so I am temporarily avoiding it in the mountains. And yesterday, I already took seven chapters out of the ten yuan note in my pocket and offered them to the old lady who guards the villa for her son-in-law with the girl. She is a devout Christian who prays to God and drinks holy water every day. Even if I "feel the autumn is endless," I can only endure this "long, lonely autumn night with the autumn lamp" and bury my head in the pile of books I brought to explore the ultimate questions of the universe and life to pass the month. I would rather be confined in a decadent life than engage in low-level pleasures and have my soul dominated by a philosophical executioner like Hong; I can no longer choose another path. So I fled to these mountains and forests to purge the toxins and dispel the bitterness hidden deep within my heart. I have never failed to consider that my lonely heart will become even lonelier as a result. But although it is lonely here, I can still breathe some fresh air. If I stay long in the atmosphere of powder and anesthetics, the little bit of fresh air that remains in me will also be contaminated!

R! When a person cannot actively resist fate, fate will not allow you to choose. If you lack the power of self-control, fate will completely control you.

Am I not already being subjugated by a dominant force and merely struggling weakly? A sad struggle! A despicable struggle! We cannot grow new strength within ourselves, can we? Can we? Where is the storm? Where is the lightning? Where is the sun?

When I realized that I was a voice shouting in the wilderness, I collapsed to the ground. I hope someone will call out: "Fallen comrade, get up..."

You are that person.

We must seize the power of rebirth!

Have you received Ali's letter yet? There is no need to be happy or sad. It is enough to be able to get up after falling. If the Ali of the past is dead, may it be resurrected now or in the near future!

Sinking is too terrible: whether it is sinking in the gutter, in pink dreams, or in pale muteness, it is terrible.

ph. says he is "standing on the edge," dependent on gravity. Stand on the edge, follow forward, forward! Even if it does not become a driving force.

A person who lives alone often likes to meditate. The more I meditate, the more I fall into the trap of metaphysics, and I will not be able to climb out of it.

Let's talk about our real lives. I have decided to stay here for a month. Please allow me to spend a month leisurely here. I am very willing to live with you, and I also love your loving mother and乖乖 little baby. I plan to move to your place after the end of this month if Shanghai is not an option. -- If Shanghai can't even find food for myself, the cultural fruit market can't fill my stomach either. -- Before I came here, I originally intended to go to your place, but my weak brain, now considers everything more, so I tore up a letter asking you to find a house and wrote that letter inviting you to the city to see Paulette Goddard's "Modern Times". You are busy teaching and cannot find the time. I had no way to wait for you to meet and discuss. After arguing with that dogmatic person -- wasn't I just throwing a few bombs? -- I couldn't bear to be that scholar's guest anymore, so I hurriedly left that devil's den and came to these mountains and fields. Your place is a personal space, and I am afraid it is not suitable for me to live there, and I am afraid it will hinder you. So I decided to come and meet the great loneliness here.

I have been here for five days, but the house was only settled yesterday. For the first three days, I lived a simple life: at night, I slept under the stars on a bed in the small pavilion in the courtyard surrounded by vines and trees, with insects singing me lullabies. In the morning, I went to the outdoor stream to wash with ice-cold spring water, and then I climbed mountains and visited temples... Renting a house here is too expensive, and eating is also expensive. This is not a place for an unemployed vagrant like me to live, but since I've come, I'll make the best of it. Today, I bought a week's worth of food and prepared to cook for myself. There is almost nothing left in my bag.

Besides borrowing a box of books here, I brought two hundred sheets of manuscript paper. I must write down something that I can write now. That's why I'm not afraid of being lonely here. In solitude, I hope this pen is my companion, my lover.

...

Bless your mother and your child, thank them for thinking of me, kiss them for me. Don't overwork yourself, and I hope you are happy! If you can find the time, come and see your lonely friend.

Cousins

— Ms. Cao Ming

The reply that Liang Yonghong, the chief clerk of Lixing Silver Firm, gave to my seventh elder brother was as follows:

"...I am very pleased to learn of your grand ambition to go abroad (the intention of going to a foreign country), and you will surely have a bright future from now on. However, regarding the matter of lending money as you requested, due to the recent shortage of funds, it is impossible to raise the money to meet your needs. How about we consider it again after the New Year?..."

My seventh elder brother and Liang Yonghong were very close friends when they studied in the village private school. Later, they separated, but their friendship was still maintained considerably in their letters.

My seventh elder brother handed me the letter belatedly, his arm around the back of his head, his eyes reflecting a layer of blank light. He didn't say a word, pacing back and forth in my small house, often almost touching the wall with his chest before waking up and turning around.

He was already a twenty-four-year-old man, with savage muscles all over his body. His long figure seemed even more inappropriate in this small house, as if he might knock over some bulky furniture at any moment. I called out to him, comforted him, but he didn't hear me, as if someone had hit him on the head, causing him to fall into a state of near faintness.

"Don't be so foolishly trusting of that slippery fellow," he said to me sadly after a long time. "Didn't I make it clear in my letter to him that it wouldn't work after this month? If I go after the New Year, it will be the off-season. What will I do then? And how will I get by for these next few months?..."

The large eyes and wide mouth on his long face often made an unspoken expression of preparing to swallow some pain. He liked to do this when he was being cruelly manipulated.

Soon, he left my small house. After that, every time he wrote to me, I saw an unhappy face, as if he was planning something all day long. He was no longer as excited and earnest as before, telling me about his "ideal factory" that didn't have a Number One (boss) and allocated two-thirds of the profits to wages. He said that he would dedicate his life to this innocent and interesting ideal that was almost like a child's.

In the countryside, he was originally a well-known headstrong and adventurous child. Since he apprenticed for four years in a foreign-managed machine factory in Hung Hom, Hong Kong, his temperament strangely became stubborn and melancholic. He was almost unwilling to express his true intentions with straightforward words. His master (our cousin), a thin man in his late thirties, once criticized my seventh elder brother like this:

"It doesn't matter if he argues with me, or even hits me. How could I hate a cousin who hasn't come of age? But you must know that those No. 1s treat us like machines. If the workers cause them a little bit of obstruction, they have to 'repair' them!" His attitude in speaking was as steady and slow as his way of life. Experience drove his wisdom into a dark corner. He was overly cautious and worried about everything, which was completely opposite to my seventh elder brother.

"Seventh elder brother's unemployment proves that what I said was right... Now, it's time for him to have good luck. It's much easier to make money in Siam's industry than here—"

Regarding my seventh elder brother's unemployment, he and his master had an argument. The master said that the main reason he was fired was because his temper conflicted with the power of that No. 1. But the young man stubbornly said that it was simply because business was slow, and they didn't need so many people.

My seventh elder brother often arrogantly said that his master was a useless person.

"If there's a disaster, he'll definitely be in the last group to escape..." he said.

"This kind of person isn't a bad person. He can do very good things when something happens, because he doesn't intend to harm others!" I defended our cousin. The plan to go to Siam was realized in early November of the lunar calendar.

His demeanor when he left Guangzhou was just like a child preparing to do something fun. His blood vessels jumped under his skin to show his joy and vigor. His movements couldn't be as calm as usual, his hands and feet showing excessive excitement, and his voice was louder and more unrestrained than usual. To show his composure, he deliberately pretended to be calm, comforting me as if nothing was happening:

"After I get there, as soon as I get my wages, I'll send some back to you right away. You can support yourself now, but I'm worried about your health. Don't work yourself to death. It's good to take a few days off each month...."

Regarding my seventh elder brother's travel expenses to Siam, his master only explained it to me after he left China. Their strategy was as follows:

Not long after receiving the letter from Liang Yonghong, the chief clerk of Lixing, my seventh elder brother cancelled the idea of going to Nanyang in front of him. About half a month later, he took his master—who was then acting as a more considerate petty bureaucrat—to Liang Yonghong and said in a very certain tone that they had contacted the Anti-Smoking Bureau for a speculative business that could earn double the profit in the first month, requiring 500 yuan of capital, and they were now just short of one-third of the capital... In this way, Liang Yonghong bravely admitted to this deficiency.

"Seventh brother's words are right," the small man said to me slowly. He squatted on the bed, holding his knees with both hands, his fleshy nosetrils breathing unhappily, his expression as if in great pain. "Cheating? He doesn't admit that this behavior is cheating. He doesn't believe my borrowing contract, but he believes my lies. What can I do? But I believe that at most in half a year or a year, our friendship can be restored. Ah, that young man! He's as brave as a bear. I've never seen anyone so sure of everything he thinks." He paused to focus his mind a little more. "Maybe you all think I'm very ignorant and stupid? Actually, I know everything. His personality, his desires, but I am his master. In the factory, I can't let him cause trouble!... Now it's good. Let him run alone to a strange country to create his own world! Before he left, I told him many things, but he answered me with an easy smile. Let him go. How can a young man know the taste of life without banging his head bloody!..."

The day after my seventh elder brother left, the steady and melancholy skilled worker—my cousin—quietly returned to the Hung Hom factory alone.

The first letter my seventh elder brother gave me said that the first thing that surprised him after arriving in Siam was that the industry there was a hundred times more depressed than in Hong Kong. Even jobs lower than three dimes a day were impossible to find, and he, along with thousands and tens of thousands of people, stretched their necks outside the factory gates. He said that he was afraid he would have to change careers, and solemnly declared: "I will never return to my homeland if I don't make it in this lifetime—" He also said that if he couldn't find a job, he wouldn't even want to write to us.

This continued for three years, and I didn't receive his second letter. (Although he later accepted our cousin's advice and the travel expenses he sent, and returned in ragged clothes.) Now, when I think of his not writing, I also inexplicably resent him.

The Smiling Death

— Zhou Muzhai

Death is an irreversible tragedy for the person involved. Even cowardly suicide or passionate martyrdom is the same for others, except for hateful intention or indifferent unintentionality. Especially death that embraces a certain belief and carries a certain mission, towards the death of those who are the same or sympathetic. The irreversible foundation hides the hidden pain of unfulfilled heart and strength. "Exhausting oneself to the task, dying only after completion," is actually still a last resort. For the person involved, a concrete example is a will. For others, a concrete explanation is like "He died before achieving success, which made heroes' tears fill their lapsels."

However, Gorky's death can be said to be an exception, a smiling death.

Seeing victory, seeing the path to success, having full bodies, having those who follow in his footsteps, and it being so widespread, even in death, one can rest in peace.

But this is limited to the Soviet Union.

And for the Soviet Union, it is still a loss, an irreversible tragedy. Not to mention other countries.

A Spring

— Jiangdong

Is it autumn or winter.

The early morning is still like a desolate night,

Piles of fallen leaves in the woods are like graves,

The buried insects still have their last breath.

Is it winter or spring.

Rain-like mist and mist-like rain seal everything.

Lost birds hide under the eaves, looking at people in panic,

Unable to bear it after all, a group flew away with flapping sounds.

Extra Chapter on Photography

— Lingmo

I have two acquaintances who both love to play with photography. The ways these two people play are simply different. One is extremely fond of taking pictures of himself. Eight or nine out of ten of the photos he takes have himself in them. The other tries to avoid taking pictures of himself. He doesn't even have a self-timer. The photos that have him in them are all taken by others. When these two people meet, they often provide many reasons to defend their own quirks. However, quirks are mostly not consciously developed, so those defensive reasons are often just made up on the spot. Naturally, there may be a very valuable reason to explore here. And those who recognize photography as an art will immediately pull in some art theory to solve it. However, no sufficient reason can probably make either of these two people change his quirk. He naturally doesn't dislike his photos becoming works of art, but he won't do it if he has to sacrifice his quirk as the price. Anyway, it is generally permissible not to regard photography as art but as entertainment, so just continue playing as before.

Photos can be taken only for oneself to see, without any relationship with others, so treating photography as entertainment will not cause people's criticism. Or those who strive to win the artistic status of photography may feel that if everyone takes photos with this entertaining attitude, it will hinder the becoming of art in photography. But the results obtained by those who take photos for art may even be the same as those who take photos for business. Businessmen have various techniques to seek business satisfaction, but their works are often not as beautiful as the amateur's or some of the amateur's achievements that photographers love. Because of this, photography merchants now can only take half-length photos and enlarge them as their business. Art photographers, if they take care of art conditions everywhere, may not end up being used for nothing other than providing information for experts to brag to each other. In the future, if there are immortal photographic masterpieces, many may still come from the hands of players. Naturally, at that time, the players will not be able to maintain the name of players, but will have to be crowned with the title of artist.

Expecting too much from the achievements of playing will certainly greatly anger the proper artists. But fortunately, it is about photography. No matter how much you turn it around and scold the attitude of playing, even if the bad photos are bad, they will not become harmful. We certainly don't have to borrow the words that games are the original spirit of art to praise playing, but playing can never be falsely accused of having improper purposes. As long as playing is as serious as a child's play, then the meaning of playing is also quite serious. Being able to admit this considerable seriousness, within the limits of photography and machinery, is certainly not too far off. Unfortunately, other arts do not have such a clever mechanism to make basic decisions, so they are very different. When a sect forms a force and occupies orthodoxy, it will inevitably create many unjust cases, and wait for later art historians to redress them. The art historians of each era are almost just working on redressing unjust cases. But we know that no matter how far the redress goes, the orthodox faction will always become the object of research first, so there is never a lack of artists who strive for orthodoxy in each era. The problem of taking or not taking oneself in photos, if placed in other arts, may become the center of debate of an era. The question of whether or not to add figures in Chinese landscape painting is very close to this. It is true that a figure in landscape painting is often enough to affect the spirit of the whole painting, and the realistic nature in photography will never be changed by the addition or subtraction of a figure. This is very sufficient as the reason for a problem or not a problem, but the problem can always be dragged into the scope of not a problem. At this point, I hope that photography will not become an art again.

As I said, I have two acquaintances who love to play with photography. I myself have not even thought about learning this skill. This must be stated, on the one hand, to prevent kind-hearted people from worrying that I will fall into how much depravity because of stubbornly playing. If you ask me whether I am afraid of harming others even though I will not be harmed, I am not afraid. I think that those who play with photography will not change their quirks because of the theories of artists, then the above statement will naturally not cause the wavering of the artistic faction. And those who play already have their quirks as their basic reason, then the existence or non-existence of the above statement has nothing to do with it. Then why bother to say this set of empty words? Here, you can pull playing to weave charges. Usually, people like to talk about things that they don't understand very well. And photography is often unavoidable to have a relationship with us. We have a great opportunity to encounter a player photographer and an artistic photographer. And they want us to become the object of playing or the object of art. Since we, this object, are human, we are naturally unavoidable to have a reflection effect. We cannot, like the people when Western learning first came, refuse to take photos for fear of taking away our vital spirit, nor can we accept the new superstition that taking photos can remove bad luck and welcome photography. For photographers who are just playing, I can only reply with a no if I don't like to play. If I like to, I can let him play with taking pictures of cats and dogs, just like being called a horse or a cow, it doesn't matter. For artistic photographers, it can't be so simple. Maybe he intends to qualify me as a model. Since this qualification cannot be denied after it is expressed, nor can it be declared without consent. The author can usually not be responsible for the object, but the object cannot get rid of the author's involvement. If we have seen a certain type of photo title in some books and newspapers and feel chilling, we cannot help but feel a little cramped for artistic photographers.

Being a model for a rare and great artist is often an extraordinary honor. Shaw asked Rodin to sculpt his own statue, and Herlis called him very smart, knowing that his own achievements were not enough to be passed down permanently, and could also be immortalized by Rodin. Duncan was also very happy when he learned that Rodin intended to create a statue for him, and deeply regretted that it would not have the opportunity to be realized. In addition, I don't know how many ordinary people hope to be selected as a model by Rodin, or only hope for an artist who is next to Rodin, or even may become Rodin in case. But the farther away from Rodin the artist is, I am afraid that he thinks that he is very much like Rodin, and regards giving people statues as giving people a great honor. This kind of honor is really unbearable to accept. Unfortunately, honor has turned into irony, or my face is born badly. Kestona defended Goethe that Albert was written too badly. Although he was generally recognized as ignorant, he was actually very smart. Since he knew that the fact that Albert was its shadow would inevitably be explored, then that defense was indeed necessary. The ugliness written under the pen of a writer is recognized as the scars of others. Not much has become an indisputable theory. Why must the photos taken be "the correct body without error"? However, among the artists of photography, there is actually a faction that does not seek likeness, but only seeks spirit. This spirit is also the spirit of that "vital spirit"! In this way, in addition to hiding my ghost face from photography, I just hope that photography will not become an art again.

Night Market

— Xicun

This is Xidan Avenue in Beiping. Although Beiping is an ancient city, Xidan Avenue seems to have been put on an imported jacket and is slightly different from the original streets. If you really want to explore the ancient color of Beiping, you must first go to the dusty small alleys to find it. Xidan Avenue has obviously absorbed civilization from outside China. The streets here are also paved with asphalt, with tram tracks on them. Some of the storefront decorations are three-dimensional. After night falls, neon lights emit dazzling red and blue colors. Sales and large discounts on all goods are advertised everywhere. Cars come and go non-stop. This is the street of a modern city.

Xidan Avenue is bustling because there is a shopping mall here. In addition to the rows of shops, there are also cinemas, acrobatics arenas, drum-singing theaters and other entertainment places, which are very easy to attract tourists' footsteps. In the evening, although the acrobatics arena is closed, it is more lively than during the day. From the shopping mall along the east side of the street all the way to the Xidan Archway, stalls are set up one after another. This is the so-called "night market" - originally more lively than during the day. Pedestrians squeeze among the stalls, some strolling, some picking out goods they want to buy.

Recently, many bargains have been added to the night market, like what Fuji silk and XX yarn. They are piled high in front of the stalls, the color is good, and the price is cheap. One dime and a few cents to buy one foot, so cheap! Buying one foot of free cloth costs more than twenty cents. Naturally, everyone likes to buy cheap things. Without the stall owners shouting loudly to sell, customers are already filling the stalls and unable to cope with them all.

There are also some electroplated scissors, forks, spoons and other daily necessities, which are several times cheaper than local handicrafts. Since the things are exquisite and very convenient to use, only a fool would not like to buy them. As for myself, because I couldn't resist the temptation of the cheap price, I also bought a small foreign knife. This knife can cut paper and peel fruit skin, and it is shiny and bright, costing only twenty cents. It's not that I'm an amateur. Insiders can buy it for only eight cents. This kind of thing in Shanghai costs at least fifty or sixty cents at the most ordinary. In short, because this is smuggled goods, it is so cheap.

Selling sour plum soup is a new business that has been launched since the summer. Two cups cost one big coin. People shout loudly to attract customers. Rickshaw pullers, with sweat all over their bodies and faces, stop the rickshaw and throw one or two big coins to quench their thirst and relieve the heat. Sometimes they think it's not cold enough and add a little bit of shaved ice. Children's footprints often remain in this area, watching other people's good fortune and swallowing saliva into their throats.

The fruit stall business is not very good. The bananas are rotten and black, and there is no customer in sight. Apricots are divided into piles, all with piles of five big coins and piles of ten big coins. The cherries are already rotten, and there are not many customers buying one or two pounds of the yellow pears that are black and rotten.

It is the time when zongzi are on the market. The business of this food is not bad, and it is also iced in piles of ice, cool and delicious, which can greatly relieve the heat. One by one is sold out, and strings and strings are sold out. The owner's face is full of joy, and he carefully collects the remaining bamboo leaves, preparing to wrap them again tomorrow.

Selling fresh flowers and pancakes has no business, just like the newly baked sesame cakes are rarely patronized, and it is easy to not keep the feet of passersby.

The most meaningful thing is the small book stall. Some books are very old and are arranged there in a mess. Most of them are chapter novels of the Mandarin Duck Butterfly School, such as love and awakening the world, but occasionally you can find one or two rare or banned books, and you get it as if you have found a treasure, but the stall owner sells it at a great bargain without realizing it. Sometimes, you can spend eight big coins to buy a Western book worth 95 cents in US dollars.

The straw hat stalls and sock stalls have some customers, and seasonal goods always have a small road. Some customers also visit the fan sellers.

The most annoying thing is the rickshaw pullers. As soon as they see you get off the sidewalk, they scramble to solicit business: "Take a rickshaw? I'll take you. Where are you going?" Even if you shake your head, they will keep pestering you and blocking your way. As long as you say the place, they will swarm up and ask for the price. "One dime - forty coins - thirty coins - twenty-eight coins -" They ask for their own price and then lower it themselves. They will even pull a twelve-coin business, which is less than three cents in big money, but the rickshaw pullers in Shanghai will not pull a nine-copper-coin business.

Cars and trams are running, the noisy waves of sound, and the tide of people are surging in the night market until midnight, when the running of cars, the movement of people, and the transaction of goods can stop.

Bud

— Hua Rui

This ripe bud has blossomed,

Tomorrow morning, it will absorb the moist dewdrops,

And greet the beautiful sun with a smile.

Although the storm has struck,

And the ruthless wasteland,

Has buried the fallen petals,

Yet, this bud has finally bloomed again.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Idle Talk

Wuxi Monks to Receive First Aid Training

— Jia Wei

This is according to yesterday's newspaper report: The Wuxi County authorities, in order to enable all Buddhist believers in the county to cope with emergencies, plan to hold a first aid training class for monks, and have ordered the Buddhist Pure Land Society to prepare for its organization. Yesterday, the society specially convened a meeting of abbots from temples throughout the county, attended by several people, to discuss and pass the outline for first aid training for monks. All monks between the ages of eighteen and forty must receive first aid training. The training period is tentatively set at three months, and the training physicians will be provided by doctors from various hospitals in the urban area. Once preparations are complete, training can begin, it is said.

This is perhaps a somewhat satisfactory matter. Buddhism has deep-rooted historical origins within Chinese society. Historically, those who "leave home" to become monks or nuns, going up mountains and into forests, originally did so to "see through the red dust" and view everything as "emptiness." They inherently possess compassionate hearts and wish to deliver all beings. However, since they have retreated into mountains and forests and entered temples, they only wish to cultivate "purity" and enter "heaven" to become gods or immortals. Why should they care about worldly affairs and the masses of people? Just like scholar-officials who spend their days sitting in "bitter rain studios," drinking bitter tea, and talking about foxes and ghosts, paying no attention to the "universe" and "flies." However, although they possess a superhuman "spirituality," they ultimately still have a physical body. And this body, just like ordinary people, ultimately cannot transcend the natural environment and the collective of humanity—society.

Originally, who would dare deny that they are just like ordinary "people," representing a certain stratum of human society. Therefore, today, as the national crisis becomes more pressing day by day and the lives of the masses become more urgent day by day, the critical moment of life and death clearly indicates to us that it is either resistance for survival or extinction! Therefore, on the front lines of national unity against the enemy for national salvation, regardless of whether one is a farmer, worker, merchant, student, soldier, or even a monk or nun... as long as they are people who do not want to be slaves of a fallen nation, they must shoulder their sacred responsibility for national salvation. Therefore, today, the Wuxi authorities' preparation to organize monks and provide them with first aid training for emergencies is also one of the noteworthy tasks in today's preparations for resisting the enemy and saving the nation.

Isn't that so? According to reports in various newspapers on the 10th of this month, the Buddhist Association of China published statistics on temples and monks/nuns nationwide: There are more than 267,000 temples and nunneries of all sizes nationwide, with more than 738,000 monks and nuns. And provinces such as Sichuan, Henan, Jiangxi, Anhui, and Hunan are not yet included. Here, we will not discuss their religious stance and beliefs, or their relationship with today's society. However, in today's situation of life and death, if these hundreds of thousands of "transcendent" masses could also shoulder the responsibilities of an emergency, just like the monks of Wuxi, wouldn't they be a supporting force on our front lines of resisting the enemy! "Contribute one's strength and fulfill one's responsibility," this is the indispensable faith and responsibility of people in times of emergency, striving for national independence and sacrificing for the freedom of the masses! Arise, those who do not want to be slaves!

Cold Water Bath (Continued)

— Er He

In the countryside, the time for taking a cold water bath is also the time for busily picking cotton. When I parted the reeds to enter the water, I was often seen by my parents. What made me especially afraid was my mother, who would hold a hoe with a stern face, threatening to knock me down. So I had no choice but to obey her and climb ashore. After many such incidents, I finally learned to take cold water baths. I could not only swim, but also "submerge my head," (diving with my head underwater and swimming), which brought me unparalleled joy and also gave me a way to deal with my mother. For example, when my mother held a hoe to hit me, I would quickly submerge my whole body underwater, and after a while, I would emerge far away in another place. When my mother came chasing again, I would submerge my whole body underwater again, and after a while, I would emerge far away in another place. In this way, although my mother's face carried anger, she couldn't help but laugh out of joy in her heart. So I laughed too, admiring my own skills. Later, my mother felt that there would be no danger, so she stopped bothering me.

In the summer, from when the cicadas first started singing until their voices disappeared, I spent almost the whole day immersed in the water. The joy of propelling my body forward in the water with both hands was hard to describe. After eating dinner, sitting in the courtyard without any breeze, staring blankly at the moon overhead, with mosquitoes swarming around and beads of sweat seeping out of my skin, I would quietly invite my companions to immerse ourselves in the water. Breaking through the moon in the water formed shimmering, uncertain silver chains. When our feet moved, waves splashed everywhere, illuminated by the moon, and the waves also turned silver. Standing in the water, watching the surface gradually calm down, the moon also hid steadily at the bottom of the water. Tilting my head slightly, the shadow of my head was clearly imprinted on the water. Swimmers in the city would never know these kinds of pleasures, only wild children in the countryside could enjoy them. In the city, only those with money can enter the swimming pool, while in the countryside, a cold water bath in the river ditch only requires a body, and a little skill that anyone can enjoy.

Every day, in the wide ditch in front of the school gate, seeing many wild children taking cold water baths, I often think of my childhood. Now this kind of life is far away from me, and seeing these younger children only brings a slight sense of sadness. Summer has arrived, and I happen to be in the countryside again, I must take a cold water bath, I want to relive my old dream...

Remaining Sounds

The "Chinese Harmonica World" published by the Chinese Harmonica World Publishing House is edited by the famous harmonica expert Bao Mingshan and is the only harmonica music publication in our country. It has been published for more than a year, and because of its rich content and excellent printing, its sales have spread all over the country. There are also readers of the publication in foreign countries such as the Nanyang Islands, England, America, Germany, Japan, and other countries. The second issue of the second volume was published yesterday. For the sake of general readers, a large number of 100,000 basic subscribers are being solicited, and only the return postage of two corners is charged for the whole year's twelve issues. Those who wish to subscribe can send a letter to the promotion department of the publishing house in Yuncheng Lane, Anren Street, Shanghai, and it will be sent to you issue by issue. It is also heard that Mr. Bao teaches various famous harmonica tunes published in the publication on the Anding Radio Station (frequency 860) every Sunday.

The Moonlight Society expands its internal operations and widely solicits members. Anyone interested in drama and music can join. No membership fee is charged. Letters can be sent to Mr. Mao Ruijia, No. 207 Jiaozhou Road. The Xinmin News Agency, which specializes in movie, broadcasting, and song and dance news, has reportedly been revived. (Above Phoenix Sound)

Movie News

"Bloody Wedding" Performance

Unprecedented Tension and Excitement

Detective films have recently risen like a tide and are invincible. However, if there is a film that can appear on the silver screen with a brand new posture, an extraordinary theme, and unprecedented intensity, it is undoubtedly the latest authoritative production "Bloody Wedding" by Yi Hua Company. The production of this film required painstaking effort and was a glorious price obtained by all the actors from injuries, bloodshed, and great sacrifices. The film features two armored military vehicles, a large machine gun vehicle, four hundred rifles, twenty revolvers, and eight box cannons, consuming a total of 15,000 bullets, truly the most unprecedented and magnificent. Moreover, the mechanisms are layered? There are mysterious dilapidated temples, terrifying coffins, automatic walls, etc., all of which are novel and mysterious. Several intense battles are chilling and heart-pounding. The cast includes Wang Yin, Zheng Mengxia, Wang Naidong, Wang Cilong, Wei Heling, Guan Hongda, and dozens of others. Ms. Zheng Mengxia plays a female spy in the play, who is searched by detectives, threatened by bandits, and forcibly occupied by men. A weak woman, besieged on three sides, reaches the extreme of inner pain. In short, this film is truly a masterpiece that cannot be missed in the domestic silver screen. And Wang Juelong's directing skills have also surpassed his previous works. The film is scheduled to be released at the Jincheng Grand Theater starting Saturday.

Galai Zoborg and Qi En Yasan Co-Invest in "Wealthy Floating Clouds"

Nanjing Showing

Tian Han Joins Xinhua Company

Tian Han is a veteran figure with extremely high qualifications in the Chinese film industry, but for many years he has been engaged in drama and has not been involved in film. It wasn't until the rise of Lianhua Company that he began to compile film scripts again, such as "Three Modern Women" and "The Light of Motherhood," which were highly praised. Later, he also served in the newly established Yihua Company. Recently, apart from remotely leading the scriptwriting for one or two companies, there has been no closer involvement in the film industry. Suddenly, news came that Xinhua Film Company, due to the increasing intensity of its work and the completeness of its various talent groups, was only lacking complete scripts as a backup. They immediately set their sights on our old friend Tian, inviting him to serve as the director of scriptwriting. After several discussions, Mr. Tian was very happy to accept. From now on, Mr. Tian has already started his duties as the director of scriptwriting. He also said, "If I don't do it, then I won't; if I do it, then I have to take responsibility."

Tianmu Mountain Waterfall on Camera

A Fairyland in "Peach Blossom Dream"

The location for the outdoor scenes of "Peach Blossom Dream" is Tianmu Mountain, more than a hundred miles away from Hangzhou. This place is very secluded and there are no hotels. The large team of seventy or eighty people from Xinhua Company all live in temples on the mountain peaks. Tianmu Mountain is very high, so they are usually rolling in the clouds, feeling as if they are in the clouds on both sides. As for why they went all the way to Tianmu Mountain at any cost to shoot outdoor scenes? It is said that the great waterfall of Tianmu Mountain is truly spectacular. "Peach Blossom Dream" has several scenes that require filming many young girls playing in the water under the waterfall. Sixty or seventy girls, all bare-chested and showing their legs, each showing their swimming skills. This kind of mysterious and beautiful picture structure cannot be filmed without a good outdoor location. Therefore, the owner of Xinhua resolutely decided to send the outdoor shooting team to Tianmu Mountain at the cost of huge travel expenses and stayed there for twenty-three days. Because this place is surprisingly high and rarely sees the sun, the twenty-three days of delay actually only amounted to seven days of work. However, the results were truly excellent. After they arrived in Shanghai, they hurriedly screened the filmed footage, and everyone who saw it praised it, simply looking like a fairyland. This is truly the case that you only see results if you put in a lot of effort!
